When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the retaining and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are weakened, and cannot be cured by manner of cures; and you see the patient well suffering and having strong virtue, then make one great cautery on the stomach according to what was said before about the stomach's cautery, at the circulatory cautery; and three cauters around the belly subtle as each individual bone is subtle, and two cauters on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the knuckle, and one cautery on each elbow, and two small cauters on the stomach below the great one, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and composed of thick, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, then make cauters: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely behind the almecade, little by little in triangular shape, and one cautery under the belly. Two to do;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	et if you think his stomach is cooled, and the meat is not cooked, and one sees the face swelling, then the face one great fire cauterization on the stomach, as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen at all the cauterization nails; and leave the cauterization open for a long time. After cure him so that he is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut into the fleshiness called "thelul", if you scrape off the cauterized part that looks like a rasp, and then put all ablaze on the cauterized part of the fleshiness cut; and leave it so long as the cauteries come to the opening of the vein, so that the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much fleshiness, then cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of ointments, profiting until they are healed; and if you cauterize a great fire on the flesh, it will have greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an untimely wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we will tell in its place, then comes such a disease that it cannot be healed except by fire cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to someone, and is inflamed and discharges putrid matter and corrupted moistures, you must prove it thoroughly with a subtle tent, and be careful about the depth of the tent. After, scrape off the cauterized part that looks like a rasp, and pour it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and continue the cauterization until those putrid and corrupted parts are burned away, once, twice, or three times, depending on the quantity of what is needed; and beware of burning the nerves which are nearby, and the great veins. If the fistula goes into the bladder and intestine, be careful about these things, and do not make fires that are not in a well-tempered place, and think it is not perilous; after cure him so that he is healed, and if the wound is sealed and the matters have been removed for a long time, then know that the wound is entirely healed; and if the matters are not removed, know that the wound is torn and corrupted the bones at the fontanelle; and thus as one of those who we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys and great windiness, and does not take on a womanly appearance, then it is necessary that you make a fire cauterization on the kidneys from one side and the other at the nails of fire cauterization as we have said before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in a line, and they will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a fire cauterization on the outside of the part where the hair begins to grow on the pubic area, and one on each side, and each be as long as the nail of a thumb; and make one cauterization on the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauterizations be nails according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the membranes
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the membranes are cold and moist, and do not allow conception to occur, and the flowers are corrupted and their term is delayed; and when they come, one feels great pain: then it is necessary that you make three cauterizations around the mouth, as we have said for the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauterizations on the back; and let the cauterizations be nails, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the hip of the thigh, and because of this it moves out of its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and there is found the wound of the departure, so it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip of the thigh with a cauterization resembling a circle, and sign before the wound around the hip as it turns, so that the hip be inside the circle; and let the cauterizations be such as those which have been cauterized in the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not present, make three great fire cauterizations on the olive-shaped part, and let the cauterizations be as deep as all the keys; and cure him so that he is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip of the thigh, and it is from coldness and moisture, and the patient has been cured with what we have said in the division, but the cure does not hold, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of thick humors with foul pills or other good-looking pills similar to them.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards make a cauterization; and the manner of the cauterization is according to two manners: namely, together with burning medicines, and fire cauterization. Fire cauterization is according to many manners, one of which is this: that you cauterize on the hip of the thigh three triangular cauterizations in this form, and make a good depth and great size, and have between each cauterization a space equal to the thickness of a doornail, and let the cauterizations be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cauterization in the middle on the top of the hip, for which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, then cauterize at the fire of the circle that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in this manner so that the circles contain all the hip, and all the keys of the cure be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the manner in which we do in sciatica, when the pain holds in the hip and does not reach as far as the thigh or leg. And if it comes to the thigh and leg, make two cauterizations on the side where the patient says the pain is, and one cauterization on the ankle .iiij. doins away, a little bit; and let the cauterizations be knife-like, and let the fatty part of the cure be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two inches from the foot or almost there, then cauterize where they feel the pain three points or four on the "point" cauterization.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, make more of them; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then make a cauterization at the knife-like or circular cauterization, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who had a fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they were left so that the leg was completely inflamed, and the feet also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the feet. After a purging of the belly from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are together in two parts, do a fire cautery on one and on the other, according to this manner.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its regard, and if we see little who uses it; and yet all the same it is one of the good cauteries which can be suffered, and where it applies itself.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain from the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or percussion or from excessive blood evacuation, or from similar signs of cold matter expanded, none of these similarities is worth cauterizing, unless it comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be freed from fetid pills or other similar things, and that one is applied to their back, where the pain persists, three lines marked with a lead, and in each line .v. cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauterization be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see fit, make .iij. cauteries or .iiij. at the middle nail-shaped cautery in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight and narrow back when they wake up, and fear; and you find in the last vertebra of the back and in the appearance which appears above other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you can cure it, then cauterize at the point called "celcle" according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	And so the cauterization shall be applied to each part of the vertebra equally. And if you see fit, then cauterize around the vertebra at the pointed cautery .ij. lines or .iij., and let the points be close to one another. After curing, leave it as is until it is healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cauterization in gilbosity which is in spasm of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain from joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain from joints is due to moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which doctors properly call "podagre", and when it is caused by cold and medicines do not cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this manner: make many cauteries around the jointure of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary that you apply the cauterization to the face of the foot, then make a cautery at every point where one claims "point". And if pains come as far as the knee and to other joints, and this happens many times, then make three or four cauteries on each part, to all the olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, then do so, but do not keep your hand there longer than until the sparks of the caustic are burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend as far as the knee and back, administer the cauterization that we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are to the hands, make points around the wrist .ij. lines; and if there remains pain to the arms, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come as far as the shoulders or as far as the hips, cauterize each part, and do good governance to the patient and give medicines. For if you do good governance and purge phlegm, it will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the running of the suppurating boil
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the running comes in sores, and the boils descend to the groin and it is newly, then it is necessary that when you see it curing, it does not waste the day; and that he uses things which loosen the belly, so that the wind descends from his belly; after this make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the boil is repaired, and then lead him back to your side, and mark with a lead under the running sore on the bone of the elbow, and at all one sign which is similar to half a circle above the body; then apply the cautery in this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and gives off sweet scents. Then lead the boils back to their place; and have him hold your hand so that they do not return behind; and work well on the patient's hips, and put one cushion and one servant on his hips, and another on his breast which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with all your might, and hold it steady until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it again and again until you reach the bone; and be careful subtly so that the boil does not burst when you make the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that by this means the patient does not die or suffer other evils.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worth nothing. It is necessary that the cauterization of children be subtle according to their measure, and of great people also great according to their measure; after this cure the wound of the cautery with butter until the swelling is gone; after this cure other ointments until he is healthy, and have the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well bound; and it is necessary that his nourishments be diminished long enough, so that the boil does not burst when he prepares to go into chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he will want to get up, give him a well-made bandage and have it wrapped for another 40 days; and let him have good rest, that he does not work too much and beware of excessive fullness of drinking and eating, and high laughter; and when he has done this instruction, then he is entirely healed. And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the running of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When running sores come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then make one cauterization of the same kind according to its quantity, and let the third spark of the caustic be burned; after this cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancient ones have said that one must cauterize at three angles in this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but mark the first sign on the lead and make one line along the width above the running sore, and another below, and stretch your hand all around the whole nail-shaped cauterization. But the first cauterizations are lighter and more fleeting.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize with the "poins" caustic, and make the cauterizations according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, virtue, and location of twisting and pain. If he is healed by the first cauterization, that's good; if not, start another cauterization on top of it, because such cases are accustomed to require cauterizing in the member that is nearby, therefore you must make the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	A surgery.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The ulcers are helped sometimes by fire treatment with great aid, and likewise the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is in its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that corruption will prevail over all the patient, then do five cauterizations on the head: one inside the head to nine, and the other towards the forehead to the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand so long as the cauterization comes up to the bone, and until the skin peels off so that the vapors of the thick humors can issue forth; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the surgery is spread everywhere; and it is manifestly failing, then it is necessary that you cauterize those cauterizations on the head that we have said, and one cauterization in the navel, and two cauterizations on the spine of the neck, and six cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one large one on the groin and another below, and two on each shoulder; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and take care of the nerves that are on the back surface, so you do not burn them; and sometimes make a cauterization on the bone of the arm, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more I do of cauterization, the more it helps and brings benefit; and know that the patient does not feel pain during the cauterization as healthy people do, because the body is already entirely corrupted. And it is necessary that the cauterizations be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the manners of iron. Afterward, cure the place with flour mixed with honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	of swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any member and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, but it is not healed, then do cauterizations on the member according to the size and smallness of the member; and let the cauterizations be slightly entering into the flesh of the limb. Then cure with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes one makes a cautery and at the hand and foot and back, at the end of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; and notwithstanding, no one should intervene unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the art of medicine is of no use, then cauterize it with one cautery slightly deep, according to the quantity of the flesh of the limb, until the pus is removed, and its color changes; then cure with flour mixed with honey and lentils, and oil of roses and leaves of plantain, and blood of hen and blood of almond, each in a part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply to the wound until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for chancres by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When chancres come at the beginning and you see them stopping, then cauterize around it with a cauterization that seems like one circle, all around the chancre. And although wise men say that one should also make a cauterization in the middle of the chancre; and although this does not seem good to me, for I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen once or twice; and it is more proper to cauterize around it with the cauterization that is called "circumference", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati" and it delays in dying or because of the excess it produces or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, very old) and he has little blood or because of time; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauterizations that are painful; afterwards leave it thus. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through the cauterization, then heat the cauterization until it takes on its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" until the cauterizations have pierced through to the flesh, and be such cauterizations that the patient feels them outside in just such a way that the course of the corruption is alleviated. Then cure until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another type of disease exists which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a corruption of the member, for it corrupts the members just like fire corrupts dry ropes. If you see this disease in a place that can suffer both cauterization and fire together, then heat the cauterizations very slightly, small and great, according to what is needed at the place where the disease is; afterwards, cauterize all around until you have removed all the corruption, leaving nothing but what was corrupted gone. And then leave it for three days, and apply to the cauterized places a poultice with oil so that the fire's scorching effects are removed, and all corruption gone. Afterwards, cure with ointments generating flesh. If you see after three days that healthy flesh does not appear, that is good; and if it does not, then reapply the cautery to what remains of the corrupted places. And this corruption has sometimes been cured without cauterization by medicine in place of fire; but all the same, cauterization by fire is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure with medicinal water in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of boils that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that at the feet, by outward appearance, a disease called "clos" according to our intention, arises, which is a big, festering boil that wounds the foot. And the cauterization for this disease is done in two ways: by fire and by hot water. The cauterization by fire is when you heat one cauterizer as thick as a thumb nail, and make it of good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the boil from all sides, and have fine margins; afterwards, put the whole thing on top of the boil, and turn your hand around the boil until it comes to the head of the boil; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to emit corruption; then apply a poultice made of wild mallows crushed with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the boil will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the area with ointments generating flesh until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Et s'il sont convertit par defours lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d'aigue chaude;
li cure dou trembler	The cure for shakiness
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people shake from chilliness or fever quartan or another, it is necessary that you make four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the weight, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; if the shaking will cease, and the health of the cold illness will hasten.
des pustules puans	of stinking pimples
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes boils or stinking pimples appear on the bathed body or pustules that come from corrupted matter. It is necessary to make a cauterization at first when they appear, on each head of the pustule: a subtle cauterization with myrtle wood, so that the point is grasped by fire, or with long aristologe root, or with lenticular cautery. And sometimes one cauterizes them at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they do not grow any further ahead, but are broken down the superfluities from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often great hemorrhaging of blood comes from the artery that is cut off at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cauterization of a member, and similar things; and it is very grievous to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And although this happens to someone, if you hurry and put your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and hold them tightly until the blood is stilled beneath your fingers, and no more drips out; then take up the olive cauteries, many small and great ones, until they are all red; then grasp one, either large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery runs, and put it on that vein where you hold your fingers, and hold the cauterize so that the blood is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts forth when you lift your fingers off the vein, and the cauterize is extinguished, then take up quickly another of the cauterizes that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing these one after another until the blood is staunched; and beware that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, one cannot well staunch it, especially when the artery is large, unless by one of the three ways we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by a strong binding with thread, or by medicines put on which have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and held in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will instruct the patient to staunch with a tight binding of cloths or by placing burning things on it, or other similar things, unless they are not beneficial.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he does not have a mirror or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it tightly until it is staunched above the wound and above the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often when it is very cold, so that the blood may congeal and swell and be staunched; and make preparations for what he needs of cauterizers and medicines ahead.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all illnesses where it is necessary to cauterize with fire or burning medicine, and the questions and causes and preparations and forms of cauterizations; and I have placed that chapter from top to bottom, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same way so that what one wants to find may be found more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and therefore it is necessary to take greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you do not undertake foolishness. For many kinds of people come to cures. Some come from such a state with their illness that they will die quickly because of the severity of their disease and the great magnitude of their malice; and one should fear these things.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And there are those who will give you their sense and say: "Wait, I am healed"; but the disease is spiteful. It is not necessary that you consent to these people when they come to you with this manner, but rather put a greater custody on your honor than on your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely about those things of which you are certain and about which you can take and hold; and use prediction and indication in the cures of your diseases for the sake of health being converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, May Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have arranged this chapter in sections, as is before the section of cauterizers, that I have arranged from top to bottom, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often befalls children during childbirth, and when the woman holds the child's head too tightly; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness except in children, and all those that I have seen hastened death; and therefore it seems to me that it would be pointless to continue the work on such cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and the head was swelling each day until it could no longer be supported; and so much moisture accumulated that it seemed to be dead, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone above the sphenoid, between the skull and the bone; and the work is such that when the moisture is between the skull and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you make a cut in the head, making a wide incision; and it should be as long as two noses, as long as the moisture flows.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and you see signs that the commissures of the head are open on each part, and the liquid jumps forth when you press it with your hand from within, and this does not respond to you: so it is necessary to make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, extract the moisture entirely. After, close the incisions with cloths and powders, and put wine and oil, and let it be like that until the fifth day; then release it, and treat the wound with tenting and anointings, and let the head swell equally, and thus feed the patient dry meat without moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look where the opening of the abscess is, and the gathering of the liquid; for sometimes it is before; sometimes behind; sometimes to the right; and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the place where the abscess opens, and the gathering of the liquid, and the flesh as far as you are able; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and if there is bleeding of blood, so that the patient may die from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of pus
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease called "catarre" in the eye or at the liver, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last remedy is the fire cauterization with those that will cut off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them cut off, the patient must turn back his head; afterwards, rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then pull out the patient's neck with one cloth; then look where the vein bleeds, and the veins of both sides are behind the ears, and they are not responsive; then mark the veins from end to end, then cut off one and the other with a sharp spatula, two parts as far as the bone comes, and that will be through the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, push the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting as two should be across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood springs out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to sensing, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space for three fingers, then mark from end to end and cut up to the bone; and what is necessary regarding blood is to let it flow out so that it is .vi. c/, and perhaps a little more or less according to what the patient can endure, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point of the syphac, cut off what abscesses come, then strain the wound and bind, and treat with ointments until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraines come and sharp catarrhs, due to moistures of tears and heats in temples and soothed ancient forgetfulness and similar things, and it is treated by ways of medical cures and yet all this does not help, then we cut off the arteries of the temples and cauterize, as we have counted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient turns back the hairs of his temples, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is hardly responsive except in some men who are too cold; and if it is responsive, then pull out the patient's neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and raise the liquid of hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula which has this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then take it up with pincers, and separate well from the threads that are below each part; and if the artery is thin, then turn it to the point of the awl, then cut off that part according to the quantity of the two veins. For if it is not cut off, blood will not flow out entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And take out the blood of .vi. c/, up to .iii.; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a double strong silk thread, so that no bleeding will occur before the wound is healed, and blood will flow decoratively; then cut off the excess that is between the two ligatures at that same hour, and then, if you see, cauterize the area with the cutlery cauterizer up to the bone until the veins are cut; and this is the true work, if the patient has no fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For fire cauterization is aid to finish off moistures: for this reason it is more helpful against moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that you fill the place with old cotton and put on well-made tents; and when you remove them, be careful with dry medicines that produce flesh, and with tents, until he is healed; and if the artery bleeds so much as you work on it, hasten to cauterize by fire, or apply the place with vitriol and strain it with your hand until the bleeding subsides; and if you do not have this present, put your finger on the place until the bleeding ceases, and raise the place with cold water until the bleeding stops, and be strained as necessary; and what is true and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this fire cauterizer cutting to two parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to withstand more heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the cuttings are too close together, they retain their heat less well.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have one large space between the two cutters, and then when you have marked from end to end the two places, take the burning iron and apply it so that it reaches up to the bone, and cut off the vein in two places; and be separated between the two veins because they are not sewn together by this cauterization entirely; and this is the form of the cauterizer:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from the veins that are above the forehead of the head below, and medical treatment does not help, and you see the patient's face growing red, and feel a burning sensation on the forehead as if it were trembling; and the oils are hot and moist so that the hairs of the papers have fallen out, and the papers are scorched by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary to use this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	Et l'apelerent li ancien "cure contuse"; and it is that you do to the patient who has this disease the hairs on their forehead, then you make three incisions on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one incision be like two going into the forehead downwards as far as the nose, and the others two on both sides above the papers, and take care not to cut the arteries which are on both sides above the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the jawbones, and each wound should be the size of three fingers across the joint.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and you have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths to absorb the blood, then pour the spatula's edge into two parts where this shape is.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is above the temple up to the second incision; and scrape out all the membrane that is between the two cuts as far as the surface of the bone, then make another part from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	so put the instrument called "culterelle" into the first incision; and it is very well cutting on one side, and not cutting on the other side, and that's its shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the edge cutting towards the fatty tissue near the membrane, and the soft edge towards the bone, and push it until it comes to the middle incision. And cut off all the vessels that are coming down from the head into the wound as long as the incision is continuous up to what opens out of the membrane; and then make another part in the middle incision up to the other side; and then extract the blood equally, and express the place where the blood was taken; then put a cloth of old cotton into each incision, and put damp cloths soaked in vinegar, oil, and aloe on top, and take care that abscesses do not form; and on the third day release the bandage, and administer great purulence with stale water, then the ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the swelling of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes with a burning in the eyes as usual, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and weakening the sight, and the papers burnt; and the hair falling out, and the head deep in pain, and the patient is exhausted; then you know by these accidents that those matters and that burning do not come from one voice alone, but from many voices, and the true cure that is there, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is that you instruct the patient to lift their forehead, then make a large incision in the forehead and another of the same width one inch deep. Begin from the temple on the left side to the right temple, and let the incision be up to the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that are moving at mealtime; and when the bone is exposed, then absorb all the blood with a sponge, and then desiccate between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton and linen cloth there, and cover it with damp cloths soaked in vinegar and oil, and take care not to form an abscess; when it is healed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with things that make flesh inflamed.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flower and three parts of aloes, and make a poultice; and administer it to these wounds in order to inflame flesh everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the treatment of earwax
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of three things: either grains, or beasts, or pieces of rock or similar things like iron; or seeds, such as millet, beans, peas; or flowing things, such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When something that doesn't belong in the ear falls into the ear or grows there, and it's not suitable for the ear, don't let it stay there. Put the ear in the sun. If you see a stone, extract some violet oil or sesame oil, then administer an extraction; and make the patient sneeze with condiments, and stop their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and lift the ear up. Many times this cure works; and if it doesn't work, administer extractions with fine tweezers, that's the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the tweezers, that's good; if not, then administer an extraction with a fine thread of small double wire; and if it doesn't jump out in this way, then make a chain of iron and put the head of the chain or the ear canal strongly, and stop what is around the chain with beeswax so that the blood cannot enter with the chain; then treat it forcefully, for many times it works as we have said; and if it doesn't work in this way, then take glue from which birds are taken, and put in some instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and wrap a little cotton around; then press the glue on the stone or whatever it is, and treat it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't jump out from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear in such a way that an abscess forms and swells; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient well with cephalic ointment, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then sit the patient between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat or bone depends; and let the incision be like a moon, as long as you can reach the stone, then cut it out according to your ability, and suck it hastened to your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's grain that is in there and it swells, then administer an extraction; and if it can't come out, then administer one subtle spatula according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer an incision to that grain. But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	And then, when something flows into the ear, it's good for the patient to use condiment-induced sneezing first, and fill the ear with old cotton. And let it sit on top of that ear itself where the flow is. If it jumps out because of this, it's good. If not, then take many stones according to their length and lightness, and heat one end slightly; and put the patient's ear orifice into the stone, and pull out from the other side with another stone on top of the stone that's in the ear; and don't stop doing this with stone upon stone until all the flow is gone, and thus it jumps out entirely. And if you see, then take one reed, and put one end in the ear and the other end in the fire until the reed is completely burned; then do the same again with another reed until the flow is gone, just as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	En the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, such as a mouse and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body that one can feel it, then use forceps extraction; and this is the thing easier to remove which is in the ear.
