En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of lice from the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not benefit, then it is necessary to look at the ear to the sun: if any lice appear, then treat them with fine forceps; and if they do not appear, take a thread whose form this is.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it should be narrow below and wide above. And put the most subtle thread in the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering; then pull strongly on the entire thread; do this often until all the lice come out. And if they do not obey to come out, stop around the thread with cotton as I said in the stone; and if they do not jump forth as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proved in the removal of lice, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and then distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, whose form this is as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or tin, narrow below to one small hole, and wide above for distilling; and for pressing within the distillation with one instrument of well-made tin, and if you see, take a rasp and wrap it around the point pleasantly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice into the canal, and that which you see of your medicines in the thread, and the thread should be in the ear; then push down into the rasp all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or flows from the ear; and if the patient feels it inside, and it is a small pot heated over the fire so that one can distill in the ear; and take care not to let it be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some hole in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by stopping of wound, or new growth within the ear, and these stoppings sometimes occur very deep in the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes there is a small pot that fills up the hole, and it can be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes very deep, if one cannot see it, is of grievous inflammation in many dispositions, and that which can be seen requires that you put the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see apparent thickening, then work with all this spatula whose form this is.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and cutting in front and back all plain, so that it does not hurt the ear; if the thickening is of new flesh or cartilage of the ear, then hold it with fine forceps, and cut lightly, until that cartilage is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the thickening is very deep in the ear, then take a fine and light rasp and heat it slightly over the fire, then put it on the cartilage of the ear. If you sense the thickening that the patient feels pain to hear, cut lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and moisten with Egyptian balm.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and powder on vitriol broom; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you remove the tent and put another moist tent made of roset oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if hemorrhage comes from the wound, then plunge an absorbent and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the hemorrhage which are found in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This all that comes out of paper from the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to stretch with tenaille and forceps, and cut off at a spatula of its roots; then put on the place vitriol broom.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they flake off without a core, then cauterize with the lenticular cautery, and after the incision it moves; and many times repair, but no part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the Grisle (a type of wax)
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times there come out of the eyes' papers things that resemble grisle in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the work is as follows: be careful if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and this is a light thing to know; then make the opening wide, then scrape off each part lightly, then take with forceps, and cut. If you cannot cut without piercing a small piece of paper, it will not harm the patient; and if the tear is large, gather it together, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do nothing to it, for the ointment will soon restore it and bring forth flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending from the inner ear to the upper part, then turn the paper over, and extract the grandine with fine forceps, and cut and press on both sides; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it will not harm anything; and when the grandine is cut, pour salted water into the ear, and cure the place where flesh grows forth until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a grease that is produced in the films of the papier above, and this happens more often with children than with adults, and it causes great pain to their eyes; and they come with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and therefore they lie down on their faces soon, and sleep, and their papier below their eyelids is moist from the inflammation and appearance that has covered the exinach which appears in the eye. And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts their head in your hand; and then take one linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach from each part, then put it on them; and press with your fingers on both sides, so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle; then make a cut in the middle of the moisture with a spatula, cutting a slit of the width, but not more than the wound one makes to heal a vine; and make the skin very thin until you come to the exinach; and in several dispositions comes the exinach from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white grease.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Here is the translation:
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the hernia does not open at the beginning of the tear, so slightly widen the tear until it appears; then pull it as we have said, then moisten cloths in warm water and cold water, and place them on the area, and hold steady with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who break and place poultices to corrupt the moisture that remains. Then care for it until they are healed. And if the abscess becomes hot at the area, then care for it with emplasters soothing until they are healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs of paper grow, other than those that are natural, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes and cause ways of illnesses such as tears, softening of the paper, and whitening, until it is a cause of the destruction of the eyes; and there is care according to four manners: or by fire cautery together, or by medicinal water as described in the chapter on cautery, and this is done either by incision and sewing or by cauterization, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the patient's head on your shoulder; then turn the paper of oil towards your left hand; if it has converted, it is good; if not, put an awl into each thread above; and let this be at the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow among these hairs, and lead one thread above to all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs that are adjacent, all the spatula copulating from the great tear to the small; then draw out one thread, and place beneath the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth; then sign on the paper a figure of anointing, like the leaf of myrtle, and yet it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevating the paper which is divided in all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is someone who has need to cut out a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper is softened; then make all the spatula above the two lines that you have signed, and start from the great tear to the small; and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the ligature into one of the two angles of the key, then skin it entirely; then assemble the two lips with a seam made by an awl on each thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make the superfluity of threads above the two circles to all sticky things, if you see fit to do so; and if not, then have no care, and leave the seam and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without any binding or constraining things, because the paper revives at the healing of the wound and its assembly, but the seam is troublesome (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if there is another manner: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, with three separated ligatures according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut off what goes above the small threads equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are unable to hold the forceps and the things are not equal, then take an awl where it has one thread, and put it in the figure; and put another thread beside the great tear, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your two hands; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above what you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by seam, and care for it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: then it is necessary that you use what we have said about incision; but the seam in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of cauterization is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole in it according to what I have said, and then make two cauterizations by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut off the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on what goes above the paper of oil, and strain the two cauterizations from the two parties together; and let it be like this for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and decay and fall off, until it falls away by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, then cut off the excess forces; and cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper is lifted, and they will no longer prick with hair; and this is the form of the two cauterizations that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine awl, and put one thread of silk into it and make it soft and subtle; then assemble the ends and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be as long as a palm; then arrange another fine thread of silk briefly, and tie the head of the thread; then place the patient's head on your shoulder; and be below the sun so that the work is declared, for this is a subtle and gentle work; then put the awl into all the chase in the root of the adjacent hair, and make it pierce the paper quickly until you reach the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the chase, and put that hair into the chase if there is one, two, three, or more; then pull your hand away until the hairs come forth to all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then pull out the chase from below to all the thread that you have arranged, until the chase comes forth from the pores above and you see it by the sight of the eye; then pull out the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh rises; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural horse's mane, and be elevated with that which you leave, as long as it is elongated and then lift.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's purging
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or purging comes to the oil, there are two kinds: one natural and the other unnatural. And it happens suddenly from a wound, incision, or cauterization, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	Et li maniere de l'ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, and dessevre les levres de li, and met dedens tentes de lin, and la lie tant qu'elle soit sanee;
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care to ensure it does not heal unequally according to its former form; and these works that we have said are not other than remedies for this disease, so that it may return according to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is below which is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and gash and cautery and similar things; and the way of the treatment for this is that you take an awl, in which it has one double thread, and push it into the flesh, and make it pierce all the way to the right temple so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh; then lift the flesh up over the entire awl, and cut off at one spatula width.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is required, it is good; if not, then take a rasp and put it in the gash, and turn the paper, and make two gashes or incisions inside the paper; and be the holes of the two gashes at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter that has no name "one Greek"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its edges are worn down below, from what precedes the paper; then join the two severed parts with one thread of linen; then make the cure for this disease using softening medicines and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from gash or seam or cautery, then it is necessary that you make a plain incision below the hairs of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then sever between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the treatment according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare an instrument for every possible way that it may return the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary for treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden removal of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture has been done in the same way as the paper above is sewn with white of egg, and it cannot move nor perform its natural actions, then it is necessary that you put the point of a rasp underneath the paper and lift it up; and let it be so pinched, until you cut what is at the subtle spatula, which is not too worn away nor too torn, so that the patient cannot endure having the spatula too worn away or blinding the eye; and your incision, from which you remove this assembled part, should be slightly done, so that the paper may return to its natural form; and let all this assembled part heal, and sometimes do something in the water, and raise it with sweet water, and vinegar; then put between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye a moist linen cloth, and after three days use the colic remedy and similar things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the eyelash is in two manners: it is nervy and resembles a hard scaly skin, and another which is not nervy, but resembles white congealed moisture, which when one touches it with iron and cools it with pincers, cannot be handled; and both appearances begin at the great temple and grow slowly by degrees until it covers all the sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient places their head in your lap, then opens their eyes; and lifts the paper to your hand, then cools the eyelash with pincers of small double-edged scissors, and lifts it up; then take an awl, and put one hair from a horse, or ox, or buffalo, and a strong thread; and double the point of the awl a little and insert it into the eyelash, and pierce all the way to the entire awl, and tie the eyelash with a thread and lift it up, and scrape away everything that is on the side of the eyelash from the prune and the silk to the hair tip; then cut off what remains in the root of the temple at the subtle spatula and small forces, and leave the natural skin or the eyelid, so that through the incision the body's tears do not come forth as usual; and sometimes the eyelashes are only set on the needle and thread, as we have said; then scrape everything off the entire soft spatula from which is the form.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the spatula does not touch the fleshy skin and break it, and that the prune is not pierced; and after the incision, pour a little bit of boiled silk into the eye, and make a colic remedy with litargyrum, and leave it until the next day; then apply the cure for what needs to be done until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the eyelash is not nervy and you cannot insert the awl, and the needle cannot enter, then this appearance of eyelash is cured with medicines; and it grows as I have recounted in the division; and if you see it grow, then work on the patient's eye, and take a spatula slightly worn away according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the eyelash above subtly, and if you see that it does not diminish and the reason approaches, then distill from your mouth to the eye a colic remedy made of litargyrum and red colic, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other treatment according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, as if an aposteme were hot, then let it cool down, and first cure the hot aposteme until it is healed; then begin the treatment again just as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid hurts the eye by great harm, then suspend it with a needle and cut off part but not all, so that tears do not come forth; then distill into the eye red colic made of litargyrum.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows on the prunele
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Some men's skin grows red, and covers the prunele and restrains it above the paper and turns it back, and seems like a balauster rose; and the treatment is that the patient places their head in your lap, then opens their eyes, and cools all that flesh with suitable pincers for this, and sustains it by force; then cut off the first layer of skin, and go all the way cutting to the razor edge until the end, and take care not to bleed the eye during the treatment; and make the incision of the spatula as we have said in the incision of the eyelash and at the subtle spatula and small forces from which one removes the seal, just like the form after this chapter demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	et when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of silebourn or distill red pepper and similar corrosive medicines, and put cotton on top with egg white so it is sure to warm up an abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the pus starts to rise, and you doubt an abscess is hot, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do the same for all flesh removed in the oil by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you ease the cure of each weak oil by the natural way; and by the accidental way, in iron work; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that those members are bearing up to that work.
des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Those are veins that are red and are covered on the eye, and tolerate with their sight its work and weaken the eye all the time. It is necessary then for you to look at where the oil is, in which those veins are, if there is no other disease besides the vein; then coil it in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head in your hand, then suspend those veins completely around the entire circle according to your wisdom, and let the circles be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two circles by degree in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil those veins subtly with force, and remove the blood hour after hour, until you see those veins moving away from the eye; and beware that you do not touch the oil at the points of the spathous membranes, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut off those veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the oil green and red pepper to corrupt what remains from the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to coil all of it in that hour, then apply a poultice on the eye with soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and let it remain for some days until the pains are eased and you are sure of an abscess hot; then resume in this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls this "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and by hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a reason in him that you incise on the abscess, where it should die, and drain out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then receive it with all the instruments by which this form is; and it is called "aspre chief", and be made of iron to one head again, and be pointed as a file so long as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the surface of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed; and do this some times, then restore the surface with excitative medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the surface is sealed, and flesh grows, and the body of the bowstring is sealed, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not heal and is not apostemated, and bad accidents come to it, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other reason than to return the fistula to the point of the nose according to this form: and that you uncover the bone the second time by iron, and by hot medicines, and when it is uncovered, take one file according to this form, and let the iron be at 3 angles, and let the fistula be reduced to a head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then put it on the bone beneath the skin, and withdraw your hand from the eye a little, then turn back to the entire file until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the abscess by what the vein goes in if they hold their hand on their nose; and then restore the surface with dry medicines as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the surface, then the matter goes into the nose; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open and there is no obstruction to the nose or diminishment, it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal them, then apply poultices or bandages made of linen in a way that will not cause harm in order to draw out; then put on the eye a lien made from aloe, gall, and aloeswood, and then bind the eye with cloth and drapery; and the manner of the drapery is that you take soft drapery and double each one into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the amount the eye needs; then bind it tightly with a bandage and begin the poultices again in order not to cause harm; then remove the poultices and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the lien becomes moist, you should bind it very tightly; then remove the lien after a day and a night, and if you see the eye recovering, that is good; if not, then repeat the application of the emplaister, drapery, lien, and poultices until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the tearing of the vitreous humor
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the vitreous humor, then it opens and comes forth like grains of resin, and it is shocking to see; then if you see it opening, the work is such that you insert an awl into the root of the part below up to where it is above, then insert another awl where there is a double thread from the part of the eyelid; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl according to its disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and bind a part of the vitreous humor around, and tighten it well, then extract the awl and put on the eye a wet linen cloth with egg white; and let it be until the threads choose with the vitreous humor, then cure the eye with soothing things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the vitreous humor each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has great appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes from behind the eye and corrects the moisture of the albiginous and descends the eye, and enters as soon as possible; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eyebrow
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;
des aigues de l’oil	water of oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the appearances of waters in division, and what is needed to pierce; if you work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from light for the sun, and tie the healthy eye tightly shut; then put the oil paper on your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or on your right hand if the eyes are right-handed; then take in your right hand if the eyes are left-handed, or your left hand if the eyes are right-handed, the instrument called "almagda"; then place the point of the instrument below the crown by the thickness of a grain of corn in that corner of the oil near the lesser tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" properly, and turn your hand so long as it pierces into the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the prune to the end of the nourishment; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the tanned hide, and then put the instrument just above where the water is, then press down one path after another. If the water does not come out now, the patient will see it before him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After resting a little, and if the water rises the second time, place the force with the instrument, and when it is well inserted and does not rise, then extract almagda slightly by turning your hand little by little; and then put back into the water a little bit of the same gem, and leave that oil inside. Then put aside the stopped-up oil or moistened linen in rose ointment and abundance of egg yolk, and tie with the healthy oil. We, and those who are of our time, mix oncoming broth with abundance of egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, for there are some people who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctive alone, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle movement, and then put in almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a gentle sleep, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be careful to avoid all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head or turn it to the right or left, and tie him according to his disposition until three days; then release him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put back the tie on the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this during the cure or after incision now, but it is necessary that you hasten, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an aposteme comes forth, then you must release the oil before the seventh day, and address it with what soothes the aposteme; and when it is appeased, then release the sight and put on his face a small patch to cover for some time, and be there in that dark house. And then go out of the house little by little, and convert yourself into your own condition; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the land of Yrach, who told us that in his country they made someone almagda pierce, so that they could suck up the water, but although I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read it in the books of the ancients; and by chance this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them will see; and they should be made properly from earthenware.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the ends of these should be of this same subtlety, and the last in three angled corners.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the knee
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	At no time do the knee flesh or knee joints come forth as diverse, and there are some that seem like scorpions to many feet; and if it has such or it has flesh enchanted with fiery color, and if it has smooth flesh of bone color. In that then of those flesh which is smooth, and not at all enchanted, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the vinegar onto those flesh, and treat them fiercely; then pull out what you can sustain by the fine subtlety of a sharp part from one side, until you know that that flesh is completely stripped.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be pulled out, then open it with all one's subtlety and delicacy, so that nothing remains; and if without troubling oneself, or an aposteme comes forth, then cut as needed. And if they are malignant apostemes, then hasten and cauterize until the blood is stopped and all the flesh is removed, then pour wine onto the knee, and water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the knee opens and moisture comes up to the palace, know that it is healed; and if moisture does not flow as needed, know that there is flesh born in the bone above, so the instruments do not come forth to cut: then it is necessary that you put a linen thread about a finger thick, well oiled by hand, with between each knot of space one or less; and place the patient's knee on the thread at his own power, and lead it to smell until it comes into the mouth through the nose; and many times children do this in school, and it is a light thing for him who wants to make it. Then hold the chief that comes out by the nose with one hand, and the other chief that comes out by the mouth with the other hand, and know the one after the other as we are on the thread. Do this until you know that the night has corrupted that flesh; then pull out the thread, wipe off the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back on the knee just like before; do this three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of flesh; and then put a lead chain on the knee for some time until it is healed, and if he needs medicines such as those, then use them. And this is the form of the instrument to purify the chief, with which we distill oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or earthenware, resembling an open lamp, like a chain, and lead them also; and if you see, then make a closed chain, and have the instruments full to purge the chief; and have one handle on the chief to hold it when heating the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh to the neighbor
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there is a disease in the head of the neighbor which is called "tumor", and it grows and becomes large over time, so that it is visible to see; and therefore it is necessary that you make a hole at first, and remove all the fat, then put on top the fire cautery or burning medicine; and if one waits too long to do this until it is large, take heed if it is hard, of bad color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut it at all, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of gentle touch, not of bad color, and you can see that you can remove all of it, then empty the patient and the abscess without fear, and treat the wound with things soothing and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neighbor is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, more than in some men. It is necessary then that you do this for someone, if you look at whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together to a seam, and treat until it is healed; and if the lips are already detached on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape off all the parts of their crust as long as they are bleeding, then bring the two lips together to a seam, and bind, and powder upon powder with dragon's blood, and incense powder; and put on top of the powders a piece of plaster or another plaster suitable, and leave it until it is made whole by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the seam is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the seam of the belly; or by thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some men have within their lips a hard abscess like grains of millet, smaller and larger; then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut each notch, and take as pincers and cut in each part; then apply oil to the wound after the vitriolic incision, so that the blood is staunched; and then leave the wound open, and treat the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is flesh attached to the gums which the ancients call "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut at its root, and let the bow or blood flow; then put on top of the wound vitriolic powder, or other powders restraining and desiccating; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, then cut it a second time, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms for cutting.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh scabs that are ugly and unpleasant; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, as far as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth smell; it is necessary that you make the patient sit in your hands, and his jaws be in your saint, and remove the teeth or scabs as they appear, until there is nothing left; and thus do with the blackness and yellowness and jaundice and other blemishes, until they are removed; and if one removes what is at the first stage, that is good; but if not, then begin again on the second day and third day, until you have everything removed; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove, according to what the work shows, because those who use razors to clean between the teeth have different forms than those who use them to scrape off the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay the extraction as long as possible, because this should not happen at all; for it is a very high substance, so much so that one has no excuse for extracting.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is constrained to extract, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth's condition. Many times the pain would leave the patient and think that the tooth was a holy one, and make them extract the good tooth; and yet the pain does not depart at all because of this, as long as the bad abscess remains, for we have already said to do so with these saints. And when you are well certain of the tooth's condition, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth in every small crevice, very carefully to protect the gum from all sides; then move it to your hands or subtle forceps at the first point and point, until it is well extracted, then firmly hold the forceps; and the patient's hand should be in your holy place between your knees, and you should keep it still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump out, then take one of these instruments and plug it into each side lightly, and move it as you did first. And if the teeth are pierced and mangled, it is necessary that you fill them with cloths, where the perforations are; and then strain subtilly with forceps, so that it does not break while being strained; and it is necessary to carefully work around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take good heed that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, and the root will return to the patient with greater pains than the first time. And beware that you do not act like ignorant saints who, in their haste and boldness, sometimes break the cartilage and do not bring what we have recounted; but often bring great illnesses through the roots that remain, or through the cartilage they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the wound with wine or oil and vinegar; and if there is bleeding, which often happens, apply the wound with vitriolic powder; and if this does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments with which one should extract teeth first are those with long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of thick handles so that they do not bend when pulling out, and be made of well-forged iron, and be toothed to hold in place.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains at the extraction site, it is necessary that you put a moistened cotton cloth or a poultice on the wound for 1-2 days until the wound is softened, then insert the forceps called "algefri", with which the wound appears to have been licked by a surgeon; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of all these pincers, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put the instrument called "althali", which is also known as "palainche", for this reason:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be thick and large so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps over this, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, for which the forms come after this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument that has two reins, for this reason:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other fixings that are in front of the ratio of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like great pincers, for this reason:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break; and know that many instruments of the teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and wise and subtle masters find for themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of cases, and one does not break the skin or the other bones, where it can, so he searches for instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, for this reason:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then replace it with all this instrument:
