Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to the natural form of the body, and the shape is ugly, and especially in young girls, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly after the dentin, and is not in its right place, and one cannot smooth or file it: then draw a line; and if it is attached with the tooth, take this instrument of which this is the form, and it resembles a small beak, and let it be made of iron with an edge in shape.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper becomes harder and harder in a few days because of the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a similar file of this form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth little by little over a few days, so that it does not move until it is done; then make it smooth at the end to any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, then file off the roughness as much as necessary, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth in front loosen, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press down on what they eat without choking, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, but it does not work; then one must restrain them with a golden thread, for silver wire becomes green and rotten, but gold never changes; and let the thread be of medium size neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see directing the teeth, take the thread and insert it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the hooks between the teeth that are loose, as many as there are or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then re-cover the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and quietly, so that it does not move; and let your finger be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then file the hooks of the thread with pincers, assemble them, and re-point between the healthy teeth, and put it so that it does not wound the tongue; then leave it as tight as it can remain, and if it comes loose or the wire breaks, one must restrain it with another thread; if it remains and serves thus throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of directing the two healthy teeth, and the two loose ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then one puts it back in its place gradually, as we have said; and does not interfere with someone who is not wise and cautious, and at times one makes the form of a cow's bone tooth, and puts it in the place where there is a deficiency, and strains it so that it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this ligament comes from under the tongue or is natural, as one is born with it; or by accident of healed wound; and the work is such that you treat the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your own hands, and lift up the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament from the wide part, so that the tongue is dislodged from its dwelling, and if there is hardness or swelling, and it is a sudden wound, then apply an unguent and cut the ligament; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery is below; and when you have finished, raise the patient's head with rosewater and vinegar, or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and let the patient's mouth bleed every night, so that the wound cannot heal. And if there is bleeding of blood, put vitriol on the wound; and if the blood flows forth, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see that it is of foul color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards gangrene, and there is moisture, then apply an unguent and make a fine poultice, and deliver it from one side to the other; and if the wound bleeds at your work, put vitriol on it until it is stopped, then return to your work as long as you are treating all the way; then raise the patient's head with vinegar and oil, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes an abscess called "godath" comes inside the throat, and they are properly referred to as the two "amandres". And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, beware: if it is a hard aposteme of little sense and foul color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, nor for the bleeding of blood; but leave it until it dies, and then you will cut it open, or it would burst on its own; and if it is white and red, and the root is subtle, have the instrument ready to cut, but first look to see if the aposteme has calmed down and is appeased. Then have the patient sit before the sun, with their eyes closed, and press the tongue against all the instrument, in the form of which it is; and let it be of silver or tin, as delicate as scissors:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue all along this instrument and you see the abscess, then take the needle and the thread in the almond, and draw it forward above as much as you can; and leave nothing loose with the threads, then cut off the instrument so that the form is like one force; and although the head is curved, and from one place to another, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then cut off with forceps so that the form remains:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting from one part and the other part numb; and when you have cut off one of the almonds, then cut off the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, and cold and easy, and if there is bleeding, gargle the patient with vinegar, or grated pomegranate peels cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding ceases; then apply a cure until they are healed; and sometimes abscesses arise in the throat that are like the two almonds, so cut them off in the same way as the two almonds similarly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I healed a woman from an abscess that was born inside the throat, namely one small abscess; and I had well closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not expel air through the blocked conduit, nor eat or drink, and would have died if she remained like this for a day or two. The abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two stones through the two openings of the nose. I hastened then, and put a needle in one side, then drew it forward, and pulled out a large portion of pus; then refilled the other opening of the nose, and opened up her mouth and pressed her tongue; after putting the needle into those abscesses, and cut off a part, and only a small amount of blood came out; and thus was unblocked the conduit of the woman's throat, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept recurring, filling up the space I had emptied, until it became very large; then I bound it up and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it grew no more; and I left those parts, and all was as God did with them after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When swelling occurs in the vein, and it is inflated and long, it is called "perpendiculaire"; and if it is under a thick and rounded one, it is called "vein". When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the abscesses are appeased, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and the one that is rounded and not long; and if it is sanguine or has a reddish-brown color or is black, then it is necessary to avoid making an incision on it. For there is great danger for the patient. It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner I have said, of its thickness and length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press their tongue onto the instrument which we have made mention of previously; then put a needle into the vein, and pull it down, and cut off at one of the two instruments which I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural term; for if you cut too much, it causes pain to the voice, and to speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient has fear of cutting, then it is necessary that you use a trick at the cauterization so as not to cause fear. The manner of the cautery is hot water. It is that the patient puts their head in your hand, and then presses their tongue onto the instrument which we have said in the chapter on cautery, and mixes with living water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and apply the weight of this instrument, to form what appears:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place your head or have someone else hold the medicine, as the hairs of a comb, and place the instrument on all the medicine above the vein; and have the patient sit up straight on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down to the throat and cause bleeding; then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the vein, for the amount of time equal to half an hour, until you see it turn white and the medication's irritations be appeased; and if you see fit, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and insert the instrument into all the cotton in the cane above, so that the cotton rises up onto the vein; and do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait for three or five days. And if you need to start again with the medicine cautery, then restart it, and after the cautery, surround the vein with cotton wrapped in butter, and cleanse everything around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament, ysope, origanum, rue, camomille, and avronne, and similar herbs, and mix all or some of them together into one pot, and add a small amount of water, and make it boil; and let the pot be well glazed with earthy matter, and have an instrument inserted in the pot according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be of silver or copper, and one of the keys should be inserted into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the vein through the cane, until the vein is mortified; then repeat this often, until the vein dries out, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the abscess's heat, for many things happen then; and don't make it too hot except at the decline of the abscess's heat. And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put an eggshell inside the patient's head, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to oppress the mouth, and it is good care together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it appears on the throat as a bone or fishbone, or nothing at all; therefore, you must treat what you can see, and press the tongue onto the sun at the instrument's entire length, so that you can see the thing being affected; and what does not become apparent and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit while the food is cooked in their stomach; perhaps this will dislodge the stuck thing through vomiting. Or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a dry crumb of bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then re-swallow it; and when it comes up again, you can pull out what we have said; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take an instrument made of plover according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu'il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;
de la sansue de la gorge	of the sweat of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No medicine is good for the sweat, as I said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when it does not help, then look at the throat of the patient at the sun, and then press the tongue to the instrument that I told you. And if you see the sweat, so treat it with a small lancet or fine pincers that are worth it. And if this does not work, take a braided cord and put it in the throat of the patient, and then insert the hot iron end of the cord into the patient's throat and do it often. And if the patient drinks water all day, then take a full cup of cold water, and open the mouth, and spit it out without swallowing, and move it frequently with your hand; and as soon as the sweat feels the water, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not stop as we said, then suffumigate the patient with afezade at the instrument that I said in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will subside without harm. And the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot where there are hot coals, and let the cover be covered by a perforated cloth in the middle, and in that hole be the key to the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the cord in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but reaches the sweat; and the sweat will now stop, and if it does not stop, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then there is need for it to go away by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which you treat the sweat is such that when you can see it, it resembles curved pincers to enter the throat; and it has a resemblance to a doctor's beak, and has an asperity like lime, so that what it takes, it cannot let go; and behold this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to the remembrance that comes afterwards in this book, and they vary in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is similar to itself, and that is due to moisture. And the second manner is for those who are on the bone. For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the charred bone are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the pus is mature according to its completion; and there are some that it is necessary to pierce when they are hard and do not die according to their completion, such as those that come on joints. For when abscesses come on joints, and you leave them so long that they become putrid around them, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint may be corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. If the abscess is on the main limb, and you delay perforation until it is mature, it will harm the main limb; if it is on the foundation, you should pierce it as soon as it is dead; and one must not pierce a hard abscess without digestion being complete, except for that which is on the foundation, lest it become perforated and lengthened within, and a fistula forms; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the sign of perforation of the abscess when it is dead according to completion, and that is when the pain is appeased, and the departures of fever are ended, and the reduction of pain and heat, and the quieting and soothing of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you perform the perforation where it appears most prominent on the surface of the abscess, and where it opens up; and let the perforation be of sufficient length to reach through the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints, and on nerves and arteries, and in all equal parts where there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that are painful, according to the one member. And when abscesses are in charred bone, it is worth more that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, there will be lengthened the body with venom from it, and it will be full of much ordure; and by chance, the lips and the bottom parts of it may become hardened. And if there are any abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member requires. And it is necessary that you make small perforations for small abscesses, and large perforations for large abscesses, and many openings according to the appearance of the great size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut off the key, and cover; when it has become as dry leaves, and is exhausted, then it is necessary to do as one does with babes: and if there are those that are split into three angles, and if there are those whose covering is like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of the angels; and if there are those where you make a rounded shape, and other shapes and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who do not have a head, such as superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them thoroughly. And it is necessary when the abscess is large and has accumulated great pus, and you pierce it, so do not draw out all the pus in one hour, but only a part; then stop the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing more above it; do this gradually many times until the pus is gone. Likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman bearing, or small children, or old men who are decrepit. For the hopes sometimes jump with the issue of the pus, that by chance the patient may die, and you would not be aware of it. Therefore, proceed with great caution in this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, then dress the wound, and look to see if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cutting, then apply tents made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that they come together; and if you have cut off a part of the skin from the abscess and you have shaved it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or flax without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then remove it, and care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor leu decorrant par maintes fois.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: and I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Wherever small abscesses come forth from the head, they are like boils on a sheet of cloth, just as a spider's web is woven; and there are many similar ones. Some are fatty and humid, like pustules; and some are hard and stony to cut through, and one need not doubt if the artery does not make an obstruction. And the work of cutting is that you test all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", from which the form comes after, whatever it contains. For if it contains moisture, so be it poured out above the long one. And when the moisture is emptied, so scrape away without leaving any skin containing that moisture, for it will return again if you leave anything; then dip in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and linen, and fill the wound, and let it stay until the next day; and those who remain of the night. Then start again with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the night; then cure the wound with ointment as is suitable, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds a fatty night, cut along this form from above, down; and throw away your scraps, and scrape off all around, and put all your care in extracting everything that is there; and if the artery makes an obstruction, do what I told you afterwards. And do the same with the abscess if it is stony, and of cutting and curing as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting above the stony abscess and the moist one is lighter, because they are full of blood. And if there are some of these abscesses or on the head where there is no moisture, and I found one such abscess on the head of an old woman; and it was like a stony block, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if anyone had done anything to it, they would have made as much of a wound as from a stone. In other abscesses coming from the head, except those that come from the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should always remain at its most dependent part, so that the pus may issue; and cure them as is necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck and under the armpits, and sometimes in the groin area, and each one is connected to another. And each scrofula is properly contained within its own jacket, just as the night and the abscess of the head, as we said; and the similarities of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are also malicious ones that refuse to obey good health. Therefore, when you see one with a good disposition for touching, and it is similar in color to the body, and quiet on each side, and not hard against the nerves of the neck or the artery or the conduit, and not too deep; then you should cut above it, and scrape off each part, and make the two lips of the wound as thin as possible, if necessary, just as we said in abscesses of the head; and be careful not to cut the nerve or the vein, nor be too careless or hasty, lest your hand escape, and you do not see too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, so put vitriol or some powder that remains blood in the wound, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound becomes soft and begins to rot. And when the blood has stopped flowing, then return to your work, until you have completed it; then look at your duty if there are any small scrofulas remaining, and cut them and clean them. And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, it is not necessary for you to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, since there is no longer any superfluity due to the size of the scrofula. It is necessary that you understand how to cut at its root and draw it out, and sew it as we said before. Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, burst forth where they are most swollen; and burst forth in this way, depending on, then apply poultices with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with ointment bringing forth flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of gangrene
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old men said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and that is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have gangrene, it is necessary that the incision of the throat which is called "epiglote" be avoided; and one does not provide help by doing so, because all the veins and the pulsations of the patient's body are hot in those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both shoulders.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pulsation, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary therefore, when we want to cut the epiglote, that we cut it under three circles or four small incisions across, between the two circles, or according to the quantity of the abscess in the syphac, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and it is suitable for the section of the epiglote that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and swollen.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all the extent, then cuts the wound until it comes to the channel; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the abscess, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the cutting of the phlegm from the channel which bursts forth through the broken ligament, and by the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the time is passed of which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound by the key, and sew all smooth without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	All this said is that one should not do this just as long as the throat is completely filled, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the fault is being wasted.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut open the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and they are breathing through the wound, and thus is guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and therefore the ancients command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal it, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young woman take one knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut away part of the channels of the Adam's apple.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was issuing from it, and knew well that she had not cut open her jugular vein nor anything but the throat, and the blood was flowing forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and cured her until she was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happened to the young woman that she was restored to her voice, and returned to her normal state afterwards.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in cutting open the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the greenish color of jasper, and it is very common in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; or the natural one has no deceit.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fat in us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it is not necessary to operate on those that are small, and he proves and searches at every intervening point.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it just like one fat lump, and cannot be cut in any way, if you cut it, as one cuts flesh, and treat it all around, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well everywhere, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of the flesh
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many kinds of flesh are, which I will tell all the likenesses;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between flesh and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is hot and feverish, as long as the ebullition has not passed, and the corruption is accomplished; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the flesh there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains one abscess, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins just like a greenish patch, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two likenesses, either fat or moist, and many in color are such as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the flesh, that you prove and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "intermittents", according to what its form will come in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses of flesh is that you take or more moist probe than you find in the abscess, and turn your probes back and forth, until you know that the instruments have pierced the key, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the intermittent, and take care in what flows forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moist discharge is clear, whatever its color may be, then treat it as I have said about other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the intermittent there comes no more moisture, knows it is fat, then treat it thus: take pincers and pinch it lightly from each part and guard the coat where it lies, so that you may lead it out with the flesh.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot lead it out whole, then tear it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it will return the flesh many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if there remains a little bit and the blood bothers you, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders and hold it firm, and put on soothing things to hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the flesh is large, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and treat it with what nourishes flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beats against you or some other obstacle is contrary to your haste and you apply a leaden weight of vitriol, let it remain for two days or three, until the wound has purified, and the ebullition of blood subsides; then return to cutting what remains of the flesh.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Behold the forms of the intermittent instruments, and they are of three kinds: great, middle, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small, in order to search out abscesses of fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews sorceries, and they are of citrine stone, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more proven to be used for searching out the ravages of fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are of three kinds: great, middle, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the probes are of many likenesses, as you see here: great, middle, and small; and there are also probes that have two ravages of three kinds.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are probes that have three ravages, and they are also of three kinds; and there are probes that have two ravages, and single probes with only one ravage, and they are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these are cutting, and there are some that do not cut at all except from one side, by which one skins the flesh, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and from these instruments are the cloths wrapped around in strips, so that the patient does not notice at the opening of abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are of three manners: great, small, and middle-sized, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use more than in a well-oiled joint, such as knees, and arms, and shoulders, and hips, and similar joints;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling scabs of flesh, according to this form, by which blood is staunched;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the place that heals quickly from veins and arteries, and sometimes returns according to this great form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem like a woman's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, should take note according to this form of the line b from here to .g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and apply the wound with medicament letting it become dry, then bring together the two lips of the wound at the seam, and care for it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast droops down and is dimpled because of its size like that of women, then make two grooves above it, by two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	by which one is joined to the other at the end of both, so that the thicker line contains the thinner according to this form from this line b up to line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about seams and powders, and everything necessary in the treatment, until he is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if he is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not wish to rest, or due to the loss of blood, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive oil;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it so long as the remaining flesh and fat are melting, then care for it until he is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are hard forms of scrofula or there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and care for it with ointment according to this form until he is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the kind like scrofula, then do it as we have said in incisions for scrofula, and if the wound discharges pus, then apply a cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above is sealed, many times abscesses come forth, and it also happens to the vein that is swollen and abscessed.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows thus when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it at your elbow, you will feel a stiffness; and when it is due to the vein, then it appears as if it were going to burst forth.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cut this abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and hips and neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to avoid the iron treatment, and also for the one at the head, and in the one who is swollen from artery, make an incision above the long skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then operate on the size of the inch, and separate nicely the artery from the flesh, so that it is uncovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle below the one and make it pierce through to the other side, and bind the artery with a doubled thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then prick the place that is between the two ligatures with an instrument until the blood that is there issues out and the abscess is relieved.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment that brings pus, until the ligature breaks.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then care for it with ointment according to this form, until he is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the swelling of the vein, then it is necessary that you daub with your hand all that you can of the abscess to all the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle below the place that you are holding with your hand, and make it pierce through, and there will be one doubled thread, so that you can pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or the ligature of one part to the two keys of the thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will not come loose, then insert another needle under all of the thread below all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and bind the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the surplus issues out, then cut the surplus of the skin and leave what is tied.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply treatments of tents and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nails
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also just as abscesses come in the artery and vein, so too do abscesses come on the nails when they are forced, or due to excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the joints and elbows and all places where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color seems like the color of the flesh, and it is accompanied by many dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one presses strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in the depth of the body, but just below the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it is well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor above or below, and the one in the joints should not be cut with iron: perhaps there would be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and that which is on the head or forehead, make the skin at the spot.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then hold it with tweezers and cut off its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, so suspend it on the gallows, and flay it, then take out the bone and put together the wound to the seam, and let the care be until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of great haws hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it happens in bellies and not elsewhere at all the same, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" by its resemblance to ears, and it has fine roots and a thick head; and there are small and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw one person who had two of them in his belly which were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and were cut open, and inside ran with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 Z., and the works of the incision are such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the articular tissue is white and moist and of subtle root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if you cut at the spatula-like large, and be in your presence the fire cautery. For when cutting comes many times too great outflow of blood, and if the blood overflows, then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient espanting and fearful of the incision with iron, then take one good well-made cloth thread and bind the articular tissue as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the cloth thread until it cuts the articular tissue, and take care by it as much work; and if the roots are large, then you should fear to cut it yourself for the belly, but you can well cut half of it.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not reappear; then treat the wound, and be sure that you do not cut the tissue which is of a foul color and poor sense and regards milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an enchained abscess, and I will come to the treatment of chancre after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the bowel is foul
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the bowel comes from a cautery of wound or fissure of syphilis, and is on the belly and in some of the bowels, as it happens in other wounds, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the wound of syphilis and from the issue of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open to diverse issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the issue of the intestine, then it is more varied, and when one presses it to its two sides it rebounds, and then returns, and by chance it may be stuck, and greatly increases at the entrance of the bath and through great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is from moisture, it is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, not at all constraining; and if it is from blood, then it appears by these signs the abscess is great and hard, and fixed according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is from windiness, then it is tender to the toucher, and the works are such that you look to see if the appearance is from the blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	It is necessary that you leave the care. For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his linen, and be stretched out straight, then sign by encircling all around the bowel;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to sit soon between your hands
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place where you have signed at all the spatula-like
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then split the half of the abscess above to the great incision;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread or a strong silk cord tightly, and let the knot of the binding be settled.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then work on the half of the abscess stretched above the binding, and put your thumb's index finger, and probe the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught by the binding, then loosen it, and push the intestine forward out of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowel, then take it on the gallows, and cut off the superfluity;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein gives you contrary resistance, go around it well, then come back to your work and take two needles, and insert two good threads, and insert the two needles around what you have done in a cross shape as if you were piercing.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then restrain the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and let the place be such that it can heal, and take care of the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is subtle and can be done, then treat it as necessary, and shape the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as necessary, and bind the wound.
