dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likenesses of chancre, and how one should work with medicines, and how one should avoid the treatment by fire; and we say that chancre breaks out in the groin, and great caution is needed in its cure; and the ancient ones say that when chancres are in a place where they can be removed like those that are on the breast, and in the armpits, and in similar places, one should remove it all at once when it begins; and when it is large and old, then it is not necessary to approach it, for I never saw anyone heal from it; nor did anyone ever before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient with black bile at times; then make him sicker if he has manifest repletion; then bind the patient well on a good bed to perform the work; then throw away your gallows or chancre, and shape it all over, and cut it off all over leaving nothing behind; and let the blood flow freely, and press the place well with your hand or something, and if the outflow of blood makes you resistant to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then cure him with another cure until he is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division about the likenesses of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by fire: it is only lit up; and one should not touch iron on these two likenesses: namely, tympanites and hydropisophobia, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you medicate this likeness of dropsy which is called "lit up" by medicines, and the cure does not benefit, then consider if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as indigestion and similar things; so do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient with strong vigor, and they only have dropsy without any other illness, and they are neither too young nor too old, then thus work.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lay the patient right across your hands, and have the attendants press the belly from below the water to the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spoon-shaped instrument according to this form: And be cut off into two parts at a point, yet not so deep that it can come up to the intestines when you insert it, nor can it harm.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then consider if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if so, it is necessary to cut into the belly three fingers' breadth above the navel; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, then make your incision on the left side of the belly three fingers' breadth; and if it is due to bile, then make it on the right side, and do not let the patient lie over the incision so that the superfluities do not flow towards that weak part.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the entire skin with the instrument and plug it, and lift your hand to the spatula-like tool between the skin and the fatty tissue just as when shearing at the thickness of a fingernail or in a quarter; then pierce the fatty tissue until the spatula comes up to the point of view, which is the water's way, then treat the instrument so that it takes this form: And it resembles a silver thread, and it is made of lead or of light earth, and has a small pit in the lower part; and on one side, three pits; and two on the other side, and one on another; and the edges are cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that the writers shave with.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to the water, now empty it onto the instrument; then take out half or one-third part, for if you empty more than necessary at this hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of their spirit from the arm, or they may faint, or approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But empty it according to the amount of their vigor, and according to what the dispositions of their patient's vigor signify, and their pulse; then treat the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now because of the key that stops the pit which is on the fatty tissue, as I have spoken, so you pierce in this manner; then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw off a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this each day, and take care not to draw out too much water at once. And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave a great deal of water, it will be cured by heat or sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and drinking; and treat with desiccative medicines until they are healed, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the urethra
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	At no time are children born without a pit in the urethra, or the pit is small, or it is not in its place. If so, it is necessary to pierce at once each and every spatula very finely according to this form: then put the pit one fine cloth of linen, and tie it and keep it thus for three or four days, and when they wish to urinate, then remove the cloth, let them urinate, and then replace it; and by chance there is no need, because the urine that comes forth does not leave the cloth closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose pit is small will be helped by the medicine of fine cloth, as we have said, and it will expand. Those who do not have their pit in its place are harmed, because none are born with the pit at the top of the urethra, therefore they cannot urinate unless they lift up their penis; and cannot evacuate because the matter cannot come to the exit, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on their back, and then you take hold of the head of the urethra and cut it as the shape of a feather, so that the pit opens in the middle, as it should; and beware of excessive bleeding which often occurs, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops blood, and cure the wound until they are healed.
des pustules de la verge	Of the boils on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these abscesses come on the penis, and it is a foul appearance; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it is necessary that you take them to a subtle onion, and cut and clean all of them, then apply moist cotton in Egyptian ointment; then treat with divine ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess is malignant, with a foul color and pus, it is necessary that you apply fire cauterization. When you have cut it open, and the abscess is on the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is necessary that you remove the part inside first; and when it is sewn up, then treat the part outside. For if you cure them together, it is not certain that the head of the penis will not be pierced, and there will be more corruption in its own flesh and in the groin; so it is necessary to cut out everything that is black and corrupted, then apply a poultice of honey and flour made from the bark of green pomegranates and vines, then treat with other remedies until they are healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding comes from the wound, apply lunar cauterization according to this form: The cauteries help in two dispositions together: namely, at the bleeding of blood and at the corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you put a linen cloth around the penis and make the patient urinate through it; and when the skin is worn out at the head of the penis which has not been circumcised, or has been wounded or affected by aposteme, then it is necessary to cut it with a sharp instrument, so that the ligaments are loosened and the head of the penis is freed from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	et se c'est grief chose de deviser ceu, if it is a grievous thing to discuss this
de la circoncision	Of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the removal of continuity like other wounds; however when we perform this work of our own will, and properly for children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the lightest for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not circumcise their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and doctors who performed circumcision around one inch, with force, and to everything a new skin; it would be hot because there are two layers, and by chance if you cut above and leave that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Then it must be covered up, and the pain is doubled, and at the moment of skinning that part of the member is not ensured; and at the skinning of the wound by chance the iron slips out, and the work is ruined, and many times thus it happens that there is no need for skinning and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the skinning which is done with force to all the thread of wool I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally well in every way as one; but that the thread is well stretched around the skin; and the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are not doing more than just tying the thread around the penis so only, and then you let him go in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then make it stay between your hands straight and the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow or cut, and pull it up as far as the head of the penis is; then clean it well from the filth that is gathered there, then tie the signet with a double thread, then tie it below one fold to another; and hold it with two strings by the second knot at the pouch and thumb index, and cut between the two threads, then lift the cut above hastily and pull the head of the penis.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the blood run out slowly, slow and slow, for that is the mothers; and put powder on top and top a sheet glued with an egg yolk cooked with rosewater, tempered with good and fresh oil, and leave it there until the next day, and treat him with another treatment until he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the skinning is this: the two heads should be held and should be cutting, and should be the heads equally as big as the fingers equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the skinning is when the iron inside flows into the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the edges make an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot keep it at your finger, then hold it with forceps, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it exceeds three days, and what is below the penis is swollen, then leave it until the abscess has subsided, and scrape off lightly; and cut as you can move, and take care of the part of the penis, for nothing will harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound with sudden powder, which we have said or treated about powders, and if you cut too much with the iron, and it goes above, then it will not harm; then cure him as we have said, until he is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction of the stone, or frozen blood, or bowel, or flesh new, or similar things that we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to a stone in the urethra or at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees; and have his feet placed on the back, and stretch out his belly from the part above the back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can; and then force the neck of the bladder to express the stone above, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instruments called "siringue", of which this is the form: and be made of subtle silver, as thin as a bird's feather; and be the handle one and a half palms long, and be subtle at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it to the head of a piece of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread into the siringue; and cut off the excess thread and put it up to the head of the siringue, then anoint the siringue with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a stool, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and dry water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then put the siringue gently into the penis, so that it comes to the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the belly; then push the siringue forward just to the bladder, and let the patient feel come to the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless the conductor or she who guides her goes awry; then pull out the thread all along the wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out and make the urine run.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the siringue until the bladder is empty, and comfort the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcerations or blood comes into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see distilled waters and medicines, then use all the instruments called "clepsedre", and this is the form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has three perforations: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the edges are trimmed so that the medicine flows well without addition, so that it can be drawn out when needed, and inserted when necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see your medicines go into the bladder, put the head of the instrument into the moisture, and pull it back as far as it goes; then pull out the moisture with the instrument, and then push it strongly back in; then the moisture will enter and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of subtle collyrium used to purge the bladder: thus it is
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or archaute, and the head is higher; and below one side or the threads fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture that you see purging the bladder, then tie between two breasts with a good double thread, and warm half of that moisture over the fire; then fill the head of the collyrium into the vessel, then strain your hand on the bladder to all the moisture coming forth, so that the patient feels that that moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and if you don't have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make one circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put in a strong thread into these perforations, then assemble the circle as one assembles a tile, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, by pressing your hand until the moisture comes out to the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone incurred from rains, and all the signs, and in which stone one should work by size; and in the bladder, and in the vessel; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is incurred in the bladder happens more often in children, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and there appears hairiness, and the patient's member grows, and swells many times, and then becomes inflamed; and at many of these jumps the foundations are shaken; and is lighter the healing of children until they have three years, and it's very grievous in old men, and it's moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and is the cure more light for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by purging, in order to draw out all the bad blood that is at the intestines. For it sometimes hinders finding the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, and turn him over and move him down, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes falls from high up; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declining downward; then search for it and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in its place, then hurry now to cut on the stone. And if it does not fall at all when touched by all, then moisten your two middle fingers with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child; or your two median fingers, if the patient is young and completed; and fill it in its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your fingers, then guide it to the neck of the bladder; then press on your fingers and push it out to where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him that he stretches out with his right hand the intestines up high, and with his left hand takes away the skin which is below the intestines in the part where one makes the incision; then put the spatula closing, thus it is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make it between what is between the intestines and the foundation, not in the middle but alongside the left side of the naeves; and be straight on the stone, and your two fingers be at the foundation, and the incision of the traverser so that it is wide behind and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	by chance the pressure may cause the stone to jump forth with little work; and know that there are some stones which have angles, and margins: it is grievous to extract; and if there is one that is smooth, like a flint, and rounded, from which the issue is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	To that stone which has angles and margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump forth, then it is necessary to strain on the pincers that are like a file at the head, in order to grasp the stone so that it does not escape; or you put below one instrument with a subtle curved tip; and if you cannot extract it thus, then enlarge one hole slightly, and if the sand decays, then strangle it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there are more than one stone, then first extract the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut on top, then pull it forth, and the small ones afterwards if there are more. And if it is very large, then it must be split, and make a larger wound. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out immediately elsewhere than where the wound cannot heal; but still strive to extract or break with pincers, until you pull it apart piece by piece.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have completed your work, then dress the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and strain it, and put over one damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot aposteme; then resupply the patient with his collar, and do not remove the bandage until three days have passed.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, then arise very well the wound of oil and water; then treat him with diaphonic ointment and basilicon ointment, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if hot apostemes come to the wound and corroisons, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by that urine which is known in such a way that it does not jump out with the urine: then put your two fingers into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and destroy it.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound with water and oil of silex, and help him in all the ways you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works that you do to cure him, that you bind his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the leech.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the channel of the penis, and stuck inside, and the urine cannot come out; then cure him as I have said before, that you make an incision many times, or excuse yourself from making an incision for this cure. I have already proven it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod according to this shape and be fixed at three angles in one soldering:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and tie it around the penis under the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then put the rod into the penis slightly, until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand in a small hole by small hole, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis. It is soon broken, and jumps forth with the urine, and the patient is cured.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	et if you cannot do this because of anything that prevents it, then take one thread under the stone and another above, then make the rod between the two threads in place around the stone, then pull it out and release the tie, and clean up the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that the stone is lodged in women, and if it ever happens, then the cure is difficult, and it is defended by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who will reveal herself to the doctors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third way it is that perhaps one cannot find a well-informed woman in this art of surgery; and the fourth way it is that the stone of the woman is more inward than the stone of man, for which reason it requires a more profound incision, and there is great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessity requires this, then it is necessary that you take a woman who knows well, and bring her to the truth, and if you do not find one, then take at least one chaste and subtle midwife; and present to her a wise old woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you order regarding the examination of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and examine very well if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary to press her womb or foundation and seek out the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain her to place it under her womb, and command her to press her womb or the patient's womb with her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to under, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the cord, where it appears in its place, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her womb above or below the stone, and make the incision small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then press the knife into the incision, if you feel the stone so far along the wound that it can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and rounded, and those with ridges; so learn their likenesses in order to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the blood flows freely, then place vitriol powder at the site, and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding is stopped; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to help you with your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	and if the blood flows freely, and it is from the artery that was cut, then place powder on the site and strain of tents and bandages, and do not continue this, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest the patient should die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the swelling has passed, then return to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshly hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Fleshy hernia is nothing other than an accumulation of moisture or white pus, which is below the layer of the scrotum that contains the egg; and it is called "syphac", and sometimes it is properly in the lining of the egg, as if it were another egg; and this is the skin of the scrotum between the white pus that we have said; and this only happens when it does not.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this fleshy hernia is from weakness that comes to the scrotum, and it spreads this material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the scrotum, and this moisture has many colors: or it declines to yellowish, or it is without redness, or black, or water-like white, and this happens more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this accumulation, for if it is white pus that we have said, then it is a reabsorbed abscess, long and like the shape of an egg, and does not open the scrotum because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper lining, then it is a reabsorbed abscess with part of an egg, and because of this one thinks that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white pus, then one senses it well; therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, try all around the four-cornered entrance, because the shape is as we have described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what appears after the entrance, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with fire, then it is necessary that the patient be healed according to our power and the replenishment of his body; then place a poultice on his back, on something about a foot high, and put many cloths under him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and command the attendant to sit on his right side, and stretch the rod to one of the two corners of the scrotum.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula and cut the skin of the scrotum between the long and short parts, up to the groin, and make your incision entirely straight, cutting through the skin of the scrotum just to the white pus, and scrape off subtly according to our power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	then pierce the white pus with an aqueduct to one large perforation, and extract all the water, and then place your fingers, and stretch the white pus upwards; and do not touch the scrotum, but only the white pus; cut it out in pieces even if it's small, so that you don't cut too much, lest the water return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the egg comes out during your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the white pus; then assemble the two layers of the scrotum skin with a seam, and then cure it as you would other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you stop the bleeding of the vessels that are suspended; then cut off the scrotum above the suspension, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the water is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two hernias; then cut off the other part similarly to what you did with the first one, then stop the bleeding, and put a wet linen cloth soaked in rose oil into the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and place another damp wool cloth in vinegar and oil, and place on the two balls, and place above doubled cloths, and tie it above all the bandage that is according to this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and wrap them with wool yarn according to this shape and be sewn together in the belt of the breeches, and one of the ends will take up to the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the pinching; and the other chief on the two shoulders, and all assembled into the restraint of the girdle.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes medicine this thread of cautery in place of iron cutting, and it is that you take one subtle cautery knife, and cut the skin of the balls, and be heated as we have said, so that the white pitch contained in water is revealed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	so take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that pitch on the nails, and scrape it off with this subtle hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And cut it in all ways you can, until you have removed everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the yolk; and know that this work is more saving; and take care to avoid disfigurement of blood, and take heed of the works of cutting.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing else makes you contrary, or abscess forms or disfigurement of blood or anything else, then treat what makes you contrary according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, then perform a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well assured by the signs which we have said that the abscess is ripe,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	so make the patient sit on a light stool; then pierce the abscess in the lower part of the scapula as far as possible, and make the perforation long enough to reach through the entire length of the body; and be wide the hole, so that all the water can run freely.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and let the remaining water run, then treat it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not allow water to come out of the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you insert a probe or instrument used for draining the fluid from dropsical patients, as described above; and enlarge one pustule in the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or thereabouts, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the balls
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this thread there are many fears and dispositions, which is why it seems to me that it is better to leave it as it is.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and likenesses of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and indeed to the balls; and this is by many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by excessive bitterness and ague, which spreads to the balls, or from impact;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and there is no pain, and it is a grievous abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance some grievous abscesses are fearful and piercing, and of a foul color, and sometimes come from no artery or from swelling of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is by no artery, then it is known by the hot abscess disposition, when you press it to your hand.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it is not necessary that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who is caused by swelling of the vein is known by his disposition to the expression of touching with the hand.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can do well in cutting on this shape and on other bones.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the skin of the balls, then lift the yolk up high, and draw out the white pitch, and deliver the suspensory ligament from all parts of the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the yolk is already bound with these bones, then it is necessary that you draw out the yolk and the skin.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is airy within the pitch or in what is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that tension and cut it back again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the bone is in the rear, then it is necessary that you cut it all off and draw out the yolk, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, then wrap the wound in damp wool cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the balls
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enveloped in a covering similar to a bunchberry, with the softening of the balls.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and if the patient groans grievously when he walks.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment of this disease is just as fearful as the one before.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and yet we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a high stool, then tie the suspensory ligament of the balls down to your hand.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	to all the vessels that are near the penis, and tighten the master cord, and stretch them forth.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut at the scapula, cutting wide across the transverse part between the vessels, until they are uncovered.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then scrape each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein came in, and tie it again at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut them evenly in a straight line, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisters.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then treat the wound as with others that are joined in a bow, so that no vessel may bleed that nourishes one of the testicles.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for if this is not done, no harm comes from it, and if all the vessels come together, then it is necessary to draw out the testicles with all the vessels.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the sperm does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dry up and are unable to assist.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the pitch
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The events of this thread are by the section that comes from the pitch, or the extension on the belly in the part of the shoulders, which is why the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this sprain is either in the groin or from stretching it, and there are these two ways of causing it: by percussion, or by jumping, or by pulling, or by lifting a heavy load, and through similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from stretching the groin, are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal up to the very top, because the groin presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is from cutting the groin, are that it makes a sudden pain at the beginning, and there are diverse abscesses appearing under the skin close by, and this is because of the issue of the intestine and the body's reaction to the cut in the groin.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the entrails become entwined with the intestine, and it is retained there, and causes great pain to be suffered by the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments one should fear, because of which one should avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the treatment is that you instruct the patient to push his intestine back into place with his hand inside the wound, if he can get it in there;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then be steadied on his neck between your hands and lift up his hips;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then straighten the skin above and cut away all the skin of the scrotum long.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then push inside the flesh of the abdomen with a thread wound around it according to what you need to open up the wound and be such that the bone may come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape off the groin that is under the skin of the scrotum, until the white fatty tissue underneath becomes visible from all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	then place your two middle fingers in the crease where the scrotum is, between the white fatty tissue that is under the skin of the testicle and between the second groin.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and part what is behind the testicle and between the second groin; then move your right hand into the skin of the scrotum and lift up the white fatty tissue to your left hand, and lift up the testicle away from all the groin towards the belly.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the assistant to stretch the testicle upwards and to release what is behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and search with your two hands to see if the intestine has wrapped around or is entwined with the white fatty tissue, and if you find anything, then put it under the belly.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle with one thick thread made of ten threads and put it in the back part of the groin which is after the skin of the scrotum, after the belly, then cut off the hairs that appear from the threads as long as there are four threads.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then tie them together one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the groin which we have said is under the skin of the scrotum with a strong bond from two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the hairs of the threads around each other and tie them together from two parts, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter in there, lest an abscess may come.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and place the bond above it according to the first long bond of that one, and after these two bonds leave the groin which is under the skin of the scrotum a gap of about the width of a finger.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and after all the rest according to the roundness that the testicle bears; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the scrotum as long as it is sound and free from corruption, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then anoint with moistened linen dipped in oil, and put it on the wound, and apply the bond that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white fatty tissue that we have said is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and leave the bond until it falls by itself; and if it does not fall soon enough, then apply hot water, and put on what we have said, until it falls.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshly hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to do the treatment by fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients say that it is done in such a way as the branch which is together with the vine, in this manner that you tie the vessels after the belly has been slightly lifted downwards.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut into it and treat the abscess of those who work, until the vessels bleed; and then cure it as we have said, until it is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes a sprain comes in the groin, as we have said, and opens up the flesh; and none of the entrails come out to the scrotum, and if any do come out, it is little by little, and repair all hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and yet if he stays too long in this point, the wound or abscess becomes infected, to the extent that the entrails come out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens due to the stretching of the groin which is at the groin, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and swelled the flesh and opened.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the cure is done by cauterization, as we have said before; and never is cured by iron in this manner.
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and it is that the patient lies comfortably on his back between your hands, then cut away the swollen flesh of the sprain from the wide side according to the quantity of three fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the fatty tissue that is under the skin which follows, and take the raw flesh and place it on top of the apparent fatty tissue.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it to the deepest part of the belly, then sew the two apparent fleshy layers of the groin on top of the raw flesh, and sew one and the other.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the raw flesh, and do not cut anything of the groin nor stretch the testicle or any other thing, as I have made you aware in the treatment of the sprain of the entrails.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it with a wound treatment. And when you cut the threads, have someone else assist and treat the wound, until it is completely healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The groin is constricted, and has no appearance in the sprain, and the cauterization is more effective in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum becomes soft in some men, because the things that are inside are softened, and it is a sight to behold; and when one wants to treat it, one must have the patient lie on his back, and cut away the softened skin from the natural skin. Then tie the two edges together with a seam, and if you see fit, sew off the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches; then cut between the stitches, and cure it as with other wounds, until it is completely healed, and let the thread fall.
dou chastrement	The punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The punishment. Know that punishments are ordained in our law, and therefore it pleases me not to speak of them at all in this book; and it is only necessary for two purposes: one is that the physician may respond when asked and provide a cure; and the other is because we often have need to punish certain beasts to aid us, such as oxen and sheep and goats and other beasts. I say then that punishments are done in two ways: either by attraction or by incision. In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water until its testicles are softened and pliable; then we take them to hand, until they are relaxed and you no longer feel them. Regarding punishment by cutting: it is necessary that you bind the beast, and press the skin of its testicles to your left hand, then tie the suspender, and strike on each testicle once with a blow, when you have well cut them; and leave some small piece of fat and subtle fat which is above the vessels; and this manner of punishment is more effective than that done by attraction, because at attraction something remains of the testicles by chance, causing the beast to desire lust; then heal the wound until it is sound.
des hermofrodites	Of Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are according to two ways like men: one is that between the two testicles it appears as much as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair and sometimes urinates in court. And the other manner is in women, and it has on the nail as much as a penis and two testicles. And the cure for man and woman is that you cut off the parts that are joined together, and cure them like other wounds; in the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of Tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tenting is a growth attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have as much of it as a hand, and that is the cure. It is necessary that you cut off the superfluity of the tenting with your hand or fingernails, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep by fontanelle, lest blood flow forth, then cure it with another cure until it is sound; and at another growth that arises at the mouth of the womb, and swells, and perhaps jumps forth, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and for that reason they called it in olden times "cow disease". It is necessary that you cut it off as we have said about tenting, and cure it until it is sound.
de erratique	Of Erratic
