Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the womb is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to disease that has come upon it; or it's because of a growth attached to the womb, or from subtle or dense sacs, and it's made in depth in the womb, or on the sides, or below, or wherever; and it hinders conception, childbirth, and perhaps having flowers; and knowledge of this is by looking at the belly. If the stoppage is nearby apparent, it should be done to your hands or armpits. If it's from subtle sacs, and it's near two leaves, hasten and do thus: put your two hands together, and have the woman sit on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two leaves until the subtle sacs are released, and let the stoppage be overcome; then take flax, moisten it in oil, and place it on the leaf, and keep the woman at home each day, so she cannot sew. And if the sac is hard and dense, it's necessary to cut it with a spatula-like thing resembling a myrtle leaf. If the stoppage is from born flesh, suspend it at the fingernail and cut it; and have medicines that stay blood, such as alum, dragon's blood, incense, together with egg-white; then administer a wide bandage of cloth, so the wound cannot heal; and thus be long, and administer a linen tent; then be cured by other cures until it is sound. And when flesh arises in the womb, it should be cut according to this manner, unless it's an enchanted abscess. For an enchanted abscess that is in the womb, one must not touch with fire.
des emorroides	Of Hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without courtly habit, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hardened; and we have said in the division the likenesses of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive curation. I say that hemorrhoids and the hardened abscess, when they are made deep in the womb, and one cannot feel it, there is no cure by fire. Those that are at the mouth of the womb, can be felt, and they can be cured. It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then set the hardened abscess on tongs, and cut off its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, such as alum and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bathe her feet for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and apple peel and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make one poultice on her back. And if it stays, that's good. If not, make her wear ventouses on the back and breasts so as to avoid fire; then take flax, and moisten it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the wound. And when the abscess subsides, cure the wound with ointment until it is sound; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so it must be cut as I said about the hardened abscess; and then cure it until it is sound.
des apostemes de la marris	Of Abscesses of the Womb
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	There are many ways that abscesses can occur in the womb, such as chancre and piercing abscesses and herpes and ulcers and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have said in the division. It is therefore necessary for me to say about the hot abscess that occurs in the womb, which is not one of the abscesses that forms a boil. And if you want to know how to use iron, then look at whether the abscess is full of heat and fever when it first begins, and whether it becomes red if you can see it.
de l’enfantement	From childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary first to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman hastening downward, and desiring to give birth; then the child hastens to emerge; thus know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue below her head, and the secondine with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly, so that the child emerges quickly; for when it descends above her head, the secondine is with it, and the marris of its superfluities is purged by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes upon its feet, and comes forth through the body or shoulder, or hands, or it comes upon the belly, or womb, and is converted by chance on her neck, and by other bad figures; thus it is necessary for the bailiff to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out above its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her virtues are weak, then make her sit on a stool or have women hold her; and let the mixture of oil or fenugreek be cooked, and then pour it between her breasts, a little spatula-shaped thing, which is in this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And split the secondine, and cut at her umbilical cord until the moistors that are in it dry; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to purge the woman with fenugreek and oil of sesame; then make her take hold and stretch out comfortably, and keep her mouth and nose shut for an hour: thus the child is now emerging. And if both hands emerge first, it is necessary that you gently pull them back a little at a time; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up; then set the stool down on the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall down; and if the hands cannot enter and the child dies, cut the hands at the cord that is here before placed, and extract the infant, and pull it evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	From childbirth on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes out on its feet, it is necessary to support it high up;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it a little at a time, until it is even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one foot and stretch it a little at a time.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can it jump as far as the knees, if she is commanded to take hold, and make her stretch out comfortably;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps further, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not further as we have said, then turn it a little at a time, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take fenugreek of almonds, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all together in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put it on the woman's natural body inside and outside with this ointment,
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	then make her sit in hot water up to the armpits.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened beneath, make her a collar of myrrh, and put it under, and let it stay for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a stool, then make her stretch out and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press on her belly, for the child is now jumping.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From childbirth on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, then I put my hands gently around it.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then be careful of its neck, and let the feet hang down below, and be placed on a bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and bend its hands gently, then press its hands on the belly, and remove the cushions underneath, until it is prepared to come down.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then take its feet and mold them strongly, then mold the belly upwards, then put your hands in.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and gently pull the child a little at a time; and command the woman to take hold until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From childbirth when the child comes with one hand hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to contrive to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her sit on a bed, and gently lift her legs strongly.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the mixture that I have counted.
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a stool, and study how to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and gently pull the child according to the natural figure, and make her stretch out, and command her to take hold until the child emerges further.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From childbirth on its neck, with spread-out hands and face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the nurse takes its hand, then turns it gently a little at a time, and pulls it lightly.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then put on the natural mixture of fenugreek and oil, as we have said, and command her to move gently a little at a time.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	and when you have done this, then make her sit on a stool, and command her to take hold; and make her stretch out.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes forth in this manner to all the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with your finger, until the moistors are empty.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child is on its face and neck, then cut it from the mouth, so that it is not retained, and kill the child.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, as long as you have placed it so that it is necessary, and command the woman to take hold once.
adonques si istra legierement.	And then it becomes lighter.
de l’issue des gemelz	From childbirth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not an uncommon thing, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a rare thing, and do not live if they are not named.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that these two are multiplied, and are divided by the sacrum that divides them, which is attached to the mouth.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come forth naturally just like one under, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they are gentle, so let the cure be as we have said, and may the ball be subtle, and do soon and lightly what it does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thusly as is best for health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	No times are formed in the womb, i.e. one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of an infant by the measurement of divine wisdom.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is fitting that the ball knows everything, for by chance similar things happen to it;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so do according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of a dead or stillborn child, as I said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are constrained to operate with hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	so it is fitting that you know whether the woman has good health, and is not afflicted by any accident or fears death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	so it is fitting that the woman be placed on her back, and have her heels inclined downward, and her legs lifted;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister should tie a cloth of two parts around her, or she should be tied to the bed so that she is not troubled by the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then grease the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with aloes and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint your hands with these oils and these ointments.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then pour them into the womb lightly, then take one or two of those fingers that are suitable for this.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take heed whether the child is formed and descends onto its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	so insert the fingers into his eyes or in his throat or in his mouth or in his palate or under the beard or in the forehead or near the ribs.
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the descent is onto the feet, then insert or pierce and cut the membranes of the sides.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is fitting that he holds the finger in his right hand, and puts the compress between the fingers of his left hand, and pours oil all over his hand lightly, and inserts the finger into one of those places that we have said until it comes to the empty thing.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the finger;
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert another finger opposite to one another, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch them evenly by moving from one side to the other, so that the fingers are bent for movement, and are held in place as this is the form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, then anoint some of your fingers with oil and pour it into that part, and draw out the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there is none left, then place this finger or higher one, and do so until everything comes out fully.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes forward of the other, and it cannot be returned due to constriction,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	so it is fitting that you envelop on a cloth, until everything comes out.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then wrap it in the jointure of the foot or at the knee, and thus it is fitting that you do the same with the other hand, and for two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the head of the child is large and it is stretched in the issue, or it has an assembled sharp point.
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	so it is fitting that you insert a spatula between your fingers and push the head and extract the liquid.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you will round it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with instruments or chapters that are after this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus do the same if the child has a large natural head.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then draw out the bones with forceps.
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and if the head jumps forward and it is constrained to the forehead, so that they are split, until the moisture that is in the issue comes out.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, so it is fitting that you make a hole until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the extraction is gentle, and the direction to the mouth of the womb is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is stretched in the belly or at the chest, so it is fitting that you extract it onto a cloth wrapped around your hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and open the belly or chest until the moisture that is there runs.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if other limbs are removed, and the head remains.
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	so anoint your hand with oil right up to the mouth of the womb, and draw it out up to the mouth of the womb.
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then insert one or two fingers, and draw it out.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the womb is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has come there, then it is not fitting to work.
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	rather it is fitting to apply moist and greasy things.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and the emplaster should be applied in liquid, softening and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can place it evenly, then apply what we have said for a living child.
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot do so, then draw it out by pieces, and leave nothing of the placenta.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, then apply what we have said for hot abscesses that come in the womb.
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if hemorrhages of blood come, then it should be stopped with water and restrained, and other remedies applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly contained a dead child, then she consulted with another on top of it, and rejected the death of the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in her mouth, and swelled up so much that it opened, and began to cause great perturbation.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on an emplaster of strong attraction, and out came a bone, and after some days, another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly does not have bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I searched the wound and drew out many bones, until the woman was in a better state.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived for a long time like that, and would occasionally have a little bit of blood dripping from below.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I have not remembered this chapter other than for this reason that when the master finds a strange thing, he knows how to put aid there.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	and bring back the mother to her place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Next comes the shape of the pressure, with which one reads the books; and to the two turnings at the two joints of the two ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the combs should be more subtle than the restrainer, and made of ebony or boxwood.
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the wood should be one and a half feet wide, and the edge of the trees one and a half palms long.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two ligaments should be two anchors of this same wood, which are fixed in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two anchors are fitted in the mouth of the mother to open when one turns the two combs.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of wood from ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of pincers.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have at two joints two anchors, as you see, one palm long and one and a half palms wide.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you see the mother open completely with all the instrument, make the woman sit on one seat, her feet pendant and her legs outstretched.
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then insert the two anchors together into the mother, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs.
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then work your hand on the entire instrument, just as you have done with pincers evenly, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the mother, until the patient does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted and their similarities multiplied; and when the apothecaries have prepared them, then is the work more hasty and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	So do not despise the instrument that you have prepared, because their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then have her exhale slowly, and hold her hands on the mouth and navel.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps for this, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, then take a pot, and make a hole or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the mother, such as chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, cassialigna, and centoria.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put one hole or opening of the pot and the other head into the mouth of the mother.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and hold it thus until the vapors come inside the mother; then have her exhale, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the afterbirth comes out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if she remains after this treatment and is not fully healed, instruct the patient to wet her left hand with sesame oil or mullein from alethee, and then insert it into nature.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and takes the afterbirth; and when she has found it, then take it and stretch it out little by little directly, so that the mother does not harm during the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it is necessary to move slightly to the right and left, and then pull; so it will come out and be discharged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the mother is too narrow, we have said the treatment of exhaling and fumigating herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she does not accept all that we have said, then beware lest you fail to pull.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the mother, you bind to the woman's crotch, and then anoint her with ointment from tetrachamphor.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	so she will be cleansed and restored, and come forth fully; but nonetheless, when she has purged, a bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary to do fumigations suitable for this: none of the ancients have proved the fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers and the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it looks like a cord, and one puts the head of it into nature, and the wide ends over the fire.
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be above the coals, and hold it until she is satisfied, and then begin another one.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but rather it is stopped by a subtle syphac.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	So it is necessary for the patient to pierce that syphac at its root, and not pierce too deeply with a sharp spatula, and guard the ligament so she does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a moist linen in wine and oil, then the treatment with ointment until he is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop, then put in a hole a cord of cloth, and let it stay for many days, and be removed when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stoppage comes from sudden wound or abscess; so it is necessary to cover that stoppage: if it is cured, as we have said of the cloth cord.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodations, and grow larger than those that come from above the foundation or in the space between the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is one or more fistulas; and when that nodation is ancient, it works, and brings forth moisture, whitish or subtle pus.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are purulent; and are known by this that there is either emission or discharge or flatulence when the patient makes an emission, and by chance lets out one's urine.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and reach just to the joint of the crotch, and just not to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows if the fistula is purulent at the foundation, and not purulent.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you insert your two fingers or foundation, and insert a thin needle of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuousness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is tortuousness, then insert a thin piece of cloth or one hair from a horse, as far as you feel the cloth or hair to your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and there is no pus discharge nor wind nor urine, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not puncture; therefore hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends all the way to the bladder or the urinary channel, and it lets out urine, and cannot be healed by medications.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it punctures all the way to the joint of the hip, then the intestines come out at the same place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the invention of pain around it, then it is that he will come out again, and it will not be helped by medicine or healing through anointing.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these fistulas that puncture there is no cure other than surgery, and the vanity of foolish doctors who get involved with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In one that is not punctured and is not old, there is hope of recovery through iron, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift up his legs until they reach his hips, and have his hips inclined towards his stomach.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then insert a plug of clay or of lead if there is twisting, as far as you know where the intestine comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should insert your two fingers there.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	then sense that the intestine has punctured it; and be discovered where you feel between your thumb and the sac or flesh, then know that it is punctured.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if you don't intervene at all, then it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One says however that one can heal some, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid you provide is to cauterize the subtlety according to the width of the fistula, as was said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and seal it all hot in the fistula, until it reaches the fundament; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these burned edges are like a feather of a bird.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then cure it with moist tents in butter, until those edges are gone, and then cure it with anointing oil bringing forth flesh and binding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If he is thus healed, that's good. But if not, no other way can be healed.
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the intestine enters and does not puncture all the way to the thumb which is at the fundament, and between your two fingers and the intestine there is a thick covering of flesh or sac, and you see the fistula where the covering of skin ends.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	so cut from the beginning of the fistula, and seal it then before the intestine, and then apply the cauter after, as far as it reaches to the head of the intestine.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and then the intestine will be delivered and fall away; then remove those burned edges that resemble a bird's feather, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood swells up and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the cauteries of fire assemble two good things: namely, the burning away of those charred edges, and the stopping of blood and the drying up of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then cure it with moist tents in butter or in crushed hazelnuts, as long as the flesh flows forth, and let the burned edges fall away into the flow.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then cure the wound with anointing oils that bind and harden tough flesh, and are the medicines dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way to the bottom of the fundament and is far from the body, then insert your two fingers into the fundament and investigate this matter.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the intestine and it is between two layers of skin or sac or flesh, where it is near to puncturing, then there should be no doubt except for the way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it all the way down to the bottom, or if you can, put in tents and cure it as previously.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too far down in the fundament, lest you cut the tenement that holds the foundation, and the evacuations come forth involuntarily.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance if it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it when it is cut away from the fundament, either by tent or by another instrument designated.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then remove that burned edge which is in the wound, as far as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound and to keep the fistula in the part beyond the fundament: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes fistulas are according to this manner: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the fundament below the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	so take a pierced tent at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I insert one twisted thread into two, and insert the tent with all the thread into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is punctured on the edge of the fundament inside, then draw out the thread from that perforation, so that you insert your two fingers into the fundament.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull out the head of the thread, and bring together the two ends, and hold one to the other, and let it remain for one day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it at times, until the threads cut away those edges that are between two, and fall off.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not puncture, then make it puncture in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not need to be cut so far down and then cured, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spine-like spine from which one makes the fistula is very much bent in one direction and twisted.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not, because of which you should not cut what you should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of wounds
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Wounds are according to two manners: or they are inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and great ones, and in between blood flows.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have very little moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and then put it next to a little bit of yellow water or a little bit of blood, and have the same color as the body
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure for those who have them in the foundation, is that you instruct the patient to stretch and yawn frequently until the foundations become loose, and then they will appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and hold it with forceps or at your fingernail, then chop it at its roots
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the bandages cannot hold them due to their moisture, then take them from one cloth, or cotton, or a piece of cambric
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and extract them to your hands, then chop them, and powder them with some hot powders that are in place of cauterization
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cauterization, then treat them with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot come out, then purify the patient with a biting and harsh purgative to clean what is in the foundation, so that it can come out openly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	since the patient cannot feel, and if the threads are loose from the foundation, then the cure is easy.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them at your fingernail or with forceps, and chop them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and so that he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you bring the stitch together in this manner: take one twisted thread, and insert it into a needle, and then pull the thread up above and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is of a width; and hold the thread tightly, then tie the thread, and extract the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one for correcting any surplus blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put a moist cloth soaked in rose oil or cerotic on the foundation, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave him until he has had a bowel movement, and when they have ceased, then treat him with ointment and other treatments, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the putrefaction of the devil or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is putrefaction of devils in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you bring to the tip of a spatula or at your fingernail the rind above, which does not let it become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat him until he is well, as is necessary.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if he cannot be cured, then rebegin the scraping more strongly than before, until he is healed and scarred.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat him until he is healed.
dou fremit	of the tremor
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Fomice is a small, faulty appearance above the body, and goes very deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it seems to be frozen there, and one feels it also like being dead from the tremor, and comes throughout the body, more in the arms than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a cord made from an oyster's quill or a strong goose's feather, and place that cord on the tremor, until the circles mark out the tremor all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand over the entire cord until you have circled around the tremor, and push it deep, and uproot the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit, then do so with a cord of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and above, drawing it up.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	but do not pierce, in order to keep it at the two, and press down. And if you see fit, then cauterize the tremor, as is said before or in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of purgation
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a purge of silver or archaute, or melted iron or cloth; and sometimes one makes these small and large instruments, according to the way they are brought together.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then which are used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of purgation, small and great, is above wide, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has a deviation or the belly is bound, as you see, and the threads are pierced within; and has on one side two holes, and on the other one hole.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly or womb receives the medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and has between each hole one thread of espace, then insert into these holes one strong thread of twisted thread in ten or eleven turns around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, then bind with an instrument in front of a strong thread, and purify; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the purgation with oil or egg white or similar thing, then insert it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then instruct the attendants to grasp it with their two hands together, until it is fully visible, then extract the purgation, and raise the patient's legs to the appearance.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, then hold it as long as it can; and if he sleeps for a whole night afterward, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purify him in a disease of rectal obstruction, and the medicine hastens to come out, then rebegin it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the foundation or abscess, then be the purgation as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle purgation above which the skin should be strained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and from what things they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things from which wounds are made are by cutting with stone, and striking with sword and knife, or with lance or club or stick, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or those that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	I will translate the text line-by-line into English:
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a stone or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt slightly about a warm abscess: if it is healing soon itself even if it comes from the wound's blood, and the healing is on the contrary side of the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and instruct the patient to take fullness of wine and thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it does not heal, let the patient's food be reduced, and do not drink wine, nor eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply it to the wound if a warm abscess comes, with moist cotton cloth soaked only in rose oil or wine solution.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no warm abscess, put powder on the wound if it is fresh and full of blood, and not changed by air, which I will say a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the air has changed it, put some unguents on top until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the cut of a sword and similar things, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together with suturing, just as I will say for belly wounds from suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone and putrid, and only holds together by a small amount, then cut it open; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh instead of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat thick foods, such as cooked testicles and wheat, also like fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find putrid flesh and it is not attached to the bone, cut out all the putrid part and throw away the decayed matter, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has an artery in the wound or vein that is not bound by a ligature and cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it loosened, then bind it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: and that is to put this powder which cures when air has changed it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of living sulfur, and grind it subtly,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the powder to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and let it remain undisturbed unless it swells, for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one never does this with sulfur alone, unless one has no incense or dragon's blood, but only when the air has changed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the air has changed the wound, and it is in this state, then one must not put any of this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive unguents or poultices made of barley flour mixed with water and honey, until it flows freely.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, then extract it with subtle forceps;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and not put anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuance is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but make the medicine soothing, such as sulfur washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and wash it also in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and there is pus and full of discharge, then puncture or drain it lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and there comes forth a stream of blood, then open it up, and tie it off, and cauterize it if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut or the vertebrae, and the conduit is preserved, by which the flesh goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	so cut the vertebra above the canal of the throat, and do not touch the throat but leave it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it properly, and let it be for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then tie it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, then remove all that you can, and leave those that you cannot have until the wound putrifies.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let the discharge flow freely.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there are signs of windiness coming from the wound that the patient is suffering from: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder at first hour, nor bind it for the blood that does not flow deeply.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and reverts to the heart, and kills the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put an attractive unguent on it, and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have unguent, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture and fluid.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four days, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm, nor evil trembling of the heart, nor any signs of faintness from alarm.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good dispositions, then know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with tents and other remedies, until it is sound.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal or open, then know that there is a fistula; and treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is a cut from a sword or knife, and it is shallow, or deeper on one side or back, then treat what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, by stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone and has broken pieces, then close the wound and treat the burnt areas if they are raw.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not raw, then let the wound become septic, so that it will ease the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, moderate, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a great wound sometimes the intestines or the contents of the intestines protrude, for which one must introduce them;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a great one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	therefore one should insert the intestines slowly and carefully, rather than all at once;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they enter more slowly.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and therefore it is better to make the middle wound, because one should reposition the intestine to its place, rather than with the others two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches happen in the stitching of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitch for other wounds of the body and two other special stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and yet they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine protrudes,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if something needs to be returned, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or one cloth napkin in lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or boil it in water with squalin, and cypress, and spike.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and warm the intestine until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes make this wine restrain and be quiet that it only swells to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestine with water or with herbs that are cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by this it is eased the entrance to a little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is quieter than the cut.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that none should cut it without great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so cut inside in the curvature and not outside, and look at its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine protrudes forth,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	so return it to its natural shape in its proper place.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power, for this is more effective.
