Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so it is necessary that you make the patient sit on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	so put the head and breast higher than the parts below;
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two sides,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	so place your attention on that which the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to arrange what I say about great and moderate wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, put forth what appears to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then have in your hands one pitiful minister who holds all the rupture in his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that is the common manner of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave a space of about an inch at the head of the wound and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two leather thongs with the two thongs of the siphac,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is below the leather inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and bring together the two heads of the siphac in a bundle of three.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain it with a doubled thread around the needle from both sides,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then bring together the two edges of the wound smoothly,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave about an inch of space and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease to do this until you have need of the needles.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and be the needles moderate, between fine and thick.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for fine needles cut all through the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be moderate;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and leather,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	lest they cut and open the wound before the suturing;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not disturb the patient in their sleep,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or cloths on the ends of the needles to keep them steady.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is sewn.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it suffices to use one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitching is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you bring together the two leather thongs and the two thongs of the siphac in one bundle, with a needle that has a strong middle thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these holes all together four times
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	so remove the needle from the part where you started, in the way one cuts threads.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place a gap of about the thickness of a small denier between each seam.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this seam holds the flesh
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that one man had in his belly
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a knife
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's length deep.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were torn well two palms' length deep
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine and it had been out for 24 hours
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was closed in just 15 days, and I cured it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not anoint him with ointment, for I was in a place where there wasn't any to be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put a piece of old cotton on top of the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and push it through from the outside part to the inside part.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the course of right on right, so leave the end of the thread or stitch where you put in the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side through the inside part to the outside part.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the purpose of this stitching is that you stitch as tailors do with furs,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave the thread once on one side and pick it up again on the other, until the stitching is all complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of stitching, which Galen calls properly
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is as some people do who assemble the two parts together naturally
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one end of the thread to the other end in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or pick up the thread close by and make it pierce only that point.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the thread.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside part to the inside part.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the thread again.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from the outside part to the inside part, in two other points of the thread that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second way of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galens says that this phrase is true, and others bear witness to it.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with two needles, each having thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and knows that when the rupture is inside the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitching more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if the heat has changed it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestine and the flesh; then place on top a powder of burnt charcoal,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the heat has changed it, then put on some ointment that is present, until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and have the stitches and the thread tightened.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, until he is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then put on, as soon as it starts to heal, old cotton.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it two times a day until he is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine in most cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound may cause community infection to the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	so it is necessary that you moisten linen lightly with temperate heat oil or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the wounds and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or purulence in the bowels, and many times this happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then give him enemas of black wine tempered, and similarly if the purulence comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it from inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jun" cannot heal if it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it's because of the flatness of veins that they are, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the approach to its nature from hens.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine jumps out of the wound, then put it back in place just like the intestine, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become greenish or black, then it is necessary that you tie off the part that is black, so that no more blood may come from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligature,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two ends hanging from the part below the wound until it reaches the outside to ease the extraction when the intestine falls and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	one can restore it in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that one man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it was envied and became a fistula, and there came forth evacuation and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated it according to what I could do, and did not cease to subtlety until he was healed, and the wound was closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it closing, I doubted that the patient had pain in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no longer any ill, but he remained in better conditions, and eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters said that when someone has a small wound in the intestine, he must be tied in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fresh fig leaves, then bring together the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the fig leaf has opened up the mouth, then place it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if she stretches her mouth up;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he cuts the head, and this holds as long as it cannot come loose,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then puts another fold after in that manner as before, until the wound is entirely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and sews the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	That chief stays in the intestine and does not cause any harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie off the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this thread of intestine that is quite loose,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the head of this thread a fine linen thread twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then push the thread through the needle, and sew up the intestine, and tie it off in a knot;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching of flesh is not other than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the smaller intestine, there is no remedy or health, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and especially when it breaks and runs below.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the natural nodulation, hard and white, or one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it also breaks out like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes jumps high down below and at other times is thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small and at other times sufficient;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and there is no scar,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is not except through one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard scar tissue inside and on the lips that does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much pus;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the flesh is rotten and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is late in digestion and hinders health, and flees by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	or it is necessary that I inform you about the treatment for fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the spleen, or intestine, or bladder, or in some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal member, and to similar flesh.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come up to the level I have said, and you have faith in the treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you see it with your own eyes, then take a tent of iron or earth, if the fistula is straight, and sew;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, then search for a fine tent of linen,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the linen folds itself around the twisting;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it with tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	so cleanse it through one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture cuts from one opening to another and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then sew it up as well as you can, knowing if there is bone or nerve, and cut deeply enough;
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where it is located;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know truly the location of the pain, and whether it is far from a jointure, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the decayed and corrupted flesh that is inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deeply opened in the right place, then it is necessary that you cut deeply enough, as far as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put moist tents of medicated linen and tie them up to the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the excessiveness that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put in gentle oils to heal good flesh, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then let it be cauterized as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves do not bother you or the principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it away until all the corruption is removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with gentle things to heal good flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed and runs below as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	Know that you are not yet at the end:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	then uncover and sew until you reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep to come out;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	so there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature's course;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a little bit of corrupted bone and you can pull it out with forceps,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then remove them all, leaving not one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture makes it unpleasant for you and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cut and remove the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you can't remove them in an hour, then put on the wound a poultice of purifying things,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it so that the flesh is worn out around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then if they have less weight the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as that of the leg or hip,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	so just remove the corruption until the marrow is entirely removed.
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great part of the corrupt one and comes just to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	so it must be scraped and covered all around the corruption, and then cured until it is sound.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matter came to the leg and was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to delay opening it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the physician by their foolishness cut too high up that the abscess opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a great deal of matter was flowing out, and it became a fistula, and there came forth many pus-filled bubbles that all went down into the moist parts of the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many physicians put a poultice around for two years, and there was no skill in the art of healing,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so that I was called to it, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what flowed out through the pus-filled bubbles into the great body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the flesh of the young man was becoming red and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I inserted a tent in one of those abscesses, and then searched all the abscesses,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one was connected to another in all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried then, and cut into one of the abscesses until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption was coming right up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except for what I had taken away;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long period, and could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then recommenced, and found the bone just as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the corruption continued in the bone, and removed it, and then took it away, and was about to set the joint;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do so until I cut around a palm of the bone, and brought it forward to its natural state,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then restored it with medicines; and it was healed and set quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there was no need to continue the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For through the evacuation it bled often, but he was healed entirely,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and a hard flesh grew in place of the bone, and he was in good condition with no harm or opposition from anywhere, whether coming or going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be scraped in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a linen cloth and stretch it over the top of the exposed bone,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another linen cloth, larger than the first one, and tie it over the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the top, so that you bring the corrupt flesh below,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the joint where you see to scrape, so that the scraping does not wound the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a burning iron or a wooden splint under the bone to cover the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to scrape until one can see and feel the corruption, and then scrape again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	so uncover all the flesh; then put a burning iron under it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then scrape from one part to the other the corruption, and make sure the scraping is along the length of the corruption about an inch, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and scrape the bone on the other side where it contains.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuity of the two joints, then there is no other remedy except to cut it out;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand or in the toe, then that is a very strong case,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless it is necessary for you to examine this corrosion, how it appears;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve does not hinder you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and the scrapers for covering these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their coarseness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to prepare each instrument for every kind of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to your knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument you need according to what it requires.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder can be dislocated due to a reason within or due to a reason outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have tried medical treatment for that corrosion and it does not help;
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cover that member up to the point where the corruption comes,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes by these means from death or from evil, which is greater than the loss of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the members become black, as if they had been burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then pus forms after the blackness, and the corruption spreads from member to member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of everything in the body; and hurry to cover it.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if this is due to the stinging of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar creatures,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	and if the corruption is at the head of the vein, then cut it off, and do not give it any space to come all the way to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, so cut at the joint, so that the decay does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, so cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that's death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and it is not worth amending further except by the quantity of his virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so too when the decay comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then cut the whole foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up to the thigh, then cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy except to let the patient die from his sickness;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one minister to the lower tie, and another minister to the upper tie;
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you expose the flesh that is between the two ties to one broad spatula, until the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then you cut or sew, and put one linen wrap on each side, so that the seam does not touch the healthy flesh;
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another injury and abscess comes to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding comes from the wound when you work, then cauterize the flesh hastily;
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man in my time:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a boil that seemed like burning fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that decay came first to his toe of the foot, until it consumed the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the decay, he hastened to cut off the foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that, the decay came again on the toe of his hand, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things reflective after the purification of the body, and he could not cease the decays;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked that I cut off his hand, and I did not consent, because I had hope of reflecting the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he would die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the virtue of the man was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and then he hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have this tale only because it is necessary for others who make other treatment.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes on a hard skin, and stays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they burst and pierce, and the pus jumps out, and the skin remains empty, just like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is as thin as a delicate silk cloth;
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not come up to the bone, nor up to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain";
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes right to the bone and in front, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you cut around the entire skin, and similarly when it is thin, like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it is not affected by its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in front;
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and if the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a clyster thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look and see if the breast is large, and the pus that comes from it has a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then use Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take aloes, oil, and ladanum, equal parts, and put them in a vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use the clyster to treat the breast, and stop up the pus;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine sit for two hours, then strain it out slowly;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is cleansed and all pus has been removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes it is clystered with ash water;
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from grapevine, and pour water on top;
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it flow, and use it as a clyster, until you know that the breast is well cleansed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor ash water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then use a clyster of water and honey, with a little ladanum added;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you clyster it with honey and wine of honeyed grape, which the honey has the property to cleanse and wash;
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the flesh fresh;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have faith that the breast is well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then use a clyster of what makes flesh grow in it;
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and that is when you take definite plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you clyster it with some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have said or to treat ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the abscess on the breast is small, and the instrument of the clyster cannot enter it;
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then enlarge it with a little iron, and put in a tent made from Egyptian ointment;
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or Basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then sew it and leave just one place or opening for the clyster to enter;
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the abscess that pours pus is above, then cut it or lower it so that it is below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Because when the pus is in front, it does not allow flesh to remain;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut below the breast as you see;
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then arrange it in such a way that the pus flows to the lowest part of the wound.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the pus is in front, it does not allow flesh to remain;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut below the breast as you see;
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	If it is prepared in this way: that the bowstring runs smoothly downward, and leaves nothing of the bow;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to apply on the chest,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and spread one linen cloth that covers the entire chest;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut around the strong area near the breast cavity in a pouch slightly larger than the first one,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	and spread soothing oil on another cloth according to the size of the breast cavity,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the breast cavity to relieve the bowstring, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that which is on the breast cavity, is often removed in order to remove the bowstring,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what comes from the bowstring, whether it is venom or pus or enough or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been extended in this way and you see the natural discharge that springs forth on the breast cavity,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	so know that the chest is now healed and approaching health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loose it in the morning or on the third day, and when you loosen the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	you change another cloth and renew the oil.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the chest spouts undigested bowstring after many days, know that the chest is not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons depart after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health is approaching. For there are men whose flesh takes long to heal in their wounds, and of those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested bowstring springs from the chest after many days, know that the chest is not healed;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the chest takes long to heal and is far gone, then add medicines which are moist in substance and dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as defined oil, for there is a great part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take defined oil, and mix it with rose oil, and add an equal part of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then congeal it and use it; and the same makes cooked honey enlarged,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when defined oil is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and crush it, and powder it on the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then anoint with a cloth, and spread it on the chest, and at no time administer or make aristology prolonged,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lily of the valley, which is also like the flour of vetches and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use simple or compound medicines: crush them, and make powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and not cured by this remedy,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption has penetrated deeply, and makes an impression on the bone, or causes hard limbs, or joins;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	so the treatment of fistula is, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the lung
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Fungus is an abscess that arises under the armpit of the hand;
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or foot, or by chance arises in other parts;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and not taken care of, then a foul abscess comes forth,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and flows and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the lung, and by chance even all the way through;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes to corrosion just to the bone, until it brings foul pain, and is the joints of the hand wide apart, and is the color flushed.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help;
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	so it is necessary that you cut away all the excess pus that remains from the lung,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound and the lung is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the lung presses on the flesh, and begins to puncture and pierce;
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	so it is necessary that you place a cloth under the lung that pierces the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it up tight, and cut away that subtle and delicate flesh;
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply to the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with oils until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut away and remove it, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the hand corrupting, then cut away a portion of it as is said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat with oils until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed, and bound up, and it feels great pain, then it is necessary that you heal it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the lung of the spatula-like thing across on top,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and take care that the incision does not reach the flesh which is under the lung, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The joints that arise in some people's hands by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes it has a bone or a joint, and at no time an abscess;
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them are born in the root of the joint, or the birth is in certain fingers of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The one that arises in any part of the hand does not move;
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and the one that arises at the joint of the hand, by chance moves.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the shape of the one who is fleshy is light, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula-like thing.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	The one that arises in the root of the joint is hard to cure: you should hesitate to cut it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In the one that arises or is located at the back of the hand, it is necessary that you cut away the flesh all the way to the bone first.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone to a suitable thread for this, and then treat with oils until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come on the hands together come by birth, or by swelling of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut away the swelling, and then repair the hand according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or wet cloths soaked in oil rosed, so they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of plank, until the bones are joined, as is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If any swelling comes to one of his feet with the palm, then strike that swelling as is fitting.
Des vils	Of filth
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Warts are large, swollen and full of melancholy excessiveness, which come upon many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him sometimes purging with hellebore, and then the healing of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron remedy is according to two manners: one is by striking, and then drawing out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you lift the vein and draw it all forth.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting is according to this manner: arise first the leg of hot water very strongly, until the thick blood is made subtle.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then hold the patient's leg above the hip joint down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a broad stroke,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift and draw forth the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the virtues of the patient can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and command that he hold himself back from eating meat until black blood is purged out.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommence the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and it is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The application of lard is according to this manner: rise the leg of the patient if it has many hairs.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath, and rise the leg of hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat him by the fire, and then cut in the place of the vein at the long part of the knee or in the part below to the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then apply the skin to the ulcer, and scrape off the vein from each part until it appears when you touch it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems just like a white string.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then tie the thread underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then dip it in the ulcer lightly.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut in one place above three fingers; then scrape off the skin on top of the vein until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it up to the thread, just as you did, and dip it in another ulcer, just as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another stroke, or more if you need to, then lift it, and cut at the toe of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then draw it out and lift to the second stroke; then pull from stroke to stroke until it comes out all together, then cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw and lift it, then insert an awl into each strong doubled thread,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie and draw it, and put underneath one thread, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be sure that it does not cut, for if it cuts, then one cannot draw or lift it, and it comes to the patient's harm.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drawn it all out, then place a wet wool compress on the wound in vinegar and rosed oil; and dress it until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the skin is contracted and twisted and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary that you cut it obliquely, but do not cut it all the way through; and draw it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron used to cut the skin is curved, and does not cut through, so that it cuts the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of great curvature, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the form:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is situated in legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or tree, and in earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it arises in another place than in legs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes from below the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as if a serpent or worm arises within the body, and is inserted between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the limb changes and the vein begins to emerge, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the abscess opens, then it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of plank from one and a half to two and a half inches, and bind it tightly.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the plank on the leg, and every time it is not gone to the end, wrap it around the plank, and bind it tightly.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part, and wrap the remaining portion around it, and do not cut it at its root until it is all come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, then it will enter the flesh, and bring forth abscess and corruption at the place, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it is necessary that she be drawn out gradually up to the head, and nothing remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein when it is drawn out to five palms or ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me who had it issue from ten palms in length, and when you cut it, he inserted one thread or peg, and pierced it down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and the material inside is emptied, and he applies to the place medicines which prevent corruption some day, then cures it just as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein has many veins, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot or the foot itself.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there come out many pegs, and from which it jumps veins; therefore cure him just as we said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of the worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "disease of oxen", because it often affects oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes up and down throughout the body.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and he feels well when walking from member to member, until they desire the skin where it goes, and jumps further;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and he is worried about the purging of some humors, such as those that come from worms, serpents, and lumbries, or ascarides in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubts about his illness, for when he goes through the body and it rises to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance returns, and destroys the eye; and such things happen often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him being cured and treated, then one can only wait until he goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then it is necessary that you apply the oil above and below with a strong tie very tightly,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then bind on top and treat him further, and if the vein is too deep in the flesh, and you cannot find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then burn with fire above until he dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that he does is that he corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see him coming or near the eye, then hold tightly below the bone, and bind on top, and treat him further;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient with purging of bodily medicines soluble for bad humors poured out,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of foods that induce purgation.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and moves from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rise also like a worm on the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than any thing, just as bright silver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and soon after it ran throughout the body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it turned around the body again, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this disease behave in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen many others who had the same experience of their pain moving from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it before, just as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman's body was dry and her veins were uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore appeared to be a constrained windiness;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear in accordance with this reason for those who are plump, and have moist bodies and responsive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease being cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then bind above and below hastily, and then bind on top until the constrained windiness is forced out to its full extent;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and burn with fire at that place; and if you do not see it at your hands,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then treat him with those things that counteract the windiness, such as fetid pills and serpentine pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of theirs is that there are some with great points, and small ones, and hooked ones, and soldered ones;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those that have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those that fall in some member do so in two ways: either they fall in the principal member, and are hooked;
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	like brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she falls in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then it is necessary that you beware of extracting this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many dispositions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and jumps out from above the brain which is called the suture;
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is dimness of sight and numbness and swelling and redness in the head, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and mixtures of the understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without force in the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it impairs speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps from the moist white wound like boils, and also bursts forth like a boil in flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then take care of the wound and extract the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it strikes the heart is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow becomes still like a boil, and discharges black blood, and comes with coldness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know without doubt that death is certain.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow when the liver is affected is that without foam it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns pale, and he sighs deeply and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes in the covering of the ribcage, it is below the small ribs; and he spits up a great deal and suffers great pain and sighs; and all the muscles of the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes in the stomach, perhaps something from undigested food jumps out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes in the belly, and a thread of fine matter comes out through the intestines, there is no hope for cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow strikes in the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows away, and the patient feels very strong pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and neck and shoulders and aiditory and spine of the back and forceps and cuneiform bones and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you, for this reason do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man that an arrow fell onto the floor in the corner of the bedchamber at the foot of the nightstand:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to remove it and pulled it from another side under the ear fat, and it was removed without causing any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out an arrow that fell into the fatty tissue under the eyelid, beneath the parchment paper,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was stuck, and I could only grab hold of it by its tip towards the wood.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was about as long as a Turkish bow, all light iron without ears; the pull was smooth and there was no bad accident to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from a Christian's throat, and the arrow was Arabian with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I softened the feathers, and made it so fine that I pulled it out, and the Christian was saved.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from one man who had it stuck in his stomach, and I thought he was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after he had passed 30 days, his condition did not change at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and extracted it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.
