Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you find one man whose an arrow fell on his back, and the wound is sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural disposition,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you find another man whose an arrow fell on his face, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without suffering great pain; and many similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out an arrow from one of the prince's king who had it stuck in his side,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly leaning to the right part; and the arrow was entirely stuck
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the treatment after it had been stuck for three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched through all the subtle threads and did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt prickling and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the affected area an ointment that is attractive and digestive, because the swelling did not increase;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the swelling of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the ointment for many days, and the wound was healed above, and the patient remained well for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so that he felt the arrow one day inside his bedchamber; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a medicine that is corrosive by the amount of days until it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried to remove it, and felt the head of the arrow which was stuck at the point.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pushed it into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and the edges passed well over a period of three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then the wound healed so much that I put in forceps, and pulled it apart from one side and the other, and it could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not cease to soften and extract it with the means of instruments, until I pulled it out one day with well-made forceps,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to its shape as it came at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctor judged that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your treatment on what I do not say, for books cannot take everything in;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters can learn well from a small thing and from what is present and defective,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	and nine works, and nine instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out from the members where they are stuck except by two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the path where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out on the other side where it enters is an arrow entering fleshy parts and sometimes jumping out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump out now, then I leave it until the flesh is loosened around it and the exit is widened.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it's stuck in the bone and can't come out, then I leave it like that for some days and gently move it each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps out, and if it doesn't jump out, I pierce around with a very fine probe until the flesh around is widened, and then I pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said occur to the patient: so do not pull it out, but leave it until it is equalized after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes just to the brain's surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come just to the brain's surface,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, so that I gently pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's stuck very deeply and can't come out otherwise, I administer poultices around it, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is stuck in the flesh of the body where one cannot see it, then I search for it with all diligence;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein, so that I open it until the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears on the arrow to which it holds tight.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	so that the flesh that is stuck between two parts comes loose as much as you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, so you can pull it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow, but rather pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't pull it out at once, then lay it alongside the wound until it's properly prepared, then pull it out, because the extraction is eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the hemorrhage of blood makes you reluctant, then apply what we have said about treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of the incision of the nerve and vein, and make a plan how you can pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or soon or late, or firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, or if it pierces anything of the patient's body, or the skin is inflamed in that place where one can see or feel it is affected.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then above, until the forceps can take hold, and then pull it out: if it jumps forward now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it still, and then recommence the extraction until it comes out further.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the head of the arrow is stuck, then push it all the way through.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the head falls off, and you want to administer poulticing, then administer with a hairy instrument.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push it further.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is splintered, then use an instrument with a pointed end that goes in first to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, then it's necessary that you remove all the surrounding flesh where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls or lodges in the head, neck, belly, bladder, or ribcage, and it is nearby, and you can cut above, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of cutting the vein and nerve, and then pull it out, and then dress the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to remove arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and behold the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: great, small, and petty, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the hairy instrument is also like a bird's feather,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push against the point of the arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for pushing and for grasping if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the body common.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins that one uses for healing are 31, and of which there is or 16 at the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	it means to know: two jugular veins that are after the ears, which are called the "herbech".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, which are called "aspirers".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the crown of the head.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins used for healing commonly are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and the common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the femoral.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it's that one used for healing, which appears manifestly above the pocket.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saphena vein is the vein that is between the ulnar and radial veins, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the crease of the right armpit,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein that is at the ankle of the left side; and the vein called "nessel", which is on the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The healing of the veins that are after the ears helps ancient catarrh and migraine;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the healer, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and wipe the neck or veins with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's collar with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two small dependent folds from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	which then go to your throat, and where you feel the pulse beneath your throat, so it will swell.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and push it underneath the vein until it reaches the bone, then lift your hand to the entire vein above.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and open the skin and the vein well on both sides of the traverse, and make blood flow until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then tighten and bind it, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth for ancient migraine,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and sode, and ophthalmia accustomed, and to the eyes of tears aged in eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the healer are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient tightens their neck, until the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse beneath their throat, and then swells.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the key on top of the vein at your throat's index, and push the lancet underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	et lieve la voine en haut, and lift the vein upwards
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then loosen the patient, and put your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then bind it tightly, and let it be until it is healed; and I have spoken of their binding and extraction, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein on the forehead is worth just as much as the cephalic vein in ancient diseases of the face and in migraine and apoplexy.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called "fossor", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and strike with your hand or something else, and let blood flow according to the quantity you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed, and never work with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not necessary for the flames to be too thin; and the healing takes place obliquely, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The vein of the two veins that are in the temples helps with these, and with tinea, and with apoplexy, and with ophthalmia in the eye, and with diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient strains his neck by twisting in any way, just as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then bleed, and let the bleeding be from the crosswise cut, about an inch long and a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they will break; then make the blood flow until you need it, and then put it on cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The vein of the navel is worth in ague, and in sudden fever, and in diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as migraine and apoplexy that comes to the face, and indeed when it is ancient;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient strains his neck, then strains his navel to your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a long, subtle flame, and put it inside the upper lip in the space between the two nostrils.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start flowing now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and don't go too far in front, and make the blood flow according to your necessity, then bind it for a night, because it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that's the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The veins of the two groins help with the constriction of the womb, and with the beginning of menstruation, and with many diseases, and with impotence, and with corruption, and with herpes, and ulcers.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient strains his neck above one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master stand on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then bleed the long vein a little widely, then take out the blood temperately, or as much as is needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the other side in the other vein, then loosen the ligament, and strain around the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the bleeding of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins above the lips helps with hemorrhage in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and splits of lips, and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to make the patient sit before you, and strain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them by what they are black, and by what there are small black veins around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then take hold of one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then take hold of the thicker one on each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is for constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up their tongue, and looks under each side one black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then bleed one and the other, and don't go too far in front, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the shoulder that are commonly bled are bled according to two manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or in piercing all one flame mirror wide, or olive subtle as coteau trenching, and is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame mirror is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins that are smooth and full of thick blood, which contains much blood and turmoil.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and that's the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle and pointed, and is for bleeding the subtle veins, where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and on the neck, and on the chest, and on the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed moderately, and be wary of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a great deal of blood comes forth, then it is necessary to stop it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and one must not pierce the flame, but cut it like a mirror.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you exert pressure on it, and change to another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want some part of it, or you bleed in place of it the vein inside the arm: it opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut at the flame mirror, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the bleeding, then it is necessary that you strain the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulsation.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the place of the shoulder, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the armpit in vain.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not strike at the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is of the artery: then avoid.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protruding upward like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood of the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and put your thumb on top for a long time, then take away your thumb if the blood stops, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	then tie the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient's arm; and be above fear, and do not move until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and it flows, and the remedy is not present to you, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head will retreat; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a wrapping of linen, and cut it, and take one half and tie it well just to the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the blood is stopped, it's good; if not, then heal it as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping is not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound and the power of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The bloodletting from the vein in a mixture helps so much that it takes away blood from the head above and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic [veins], as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is fitting for the surgeon to beware of the nerve that is below, and if he cuts too deeply, and he finds the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the wound is grievous, and by chance cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then it is fitting that you cut the wound with an instrument vainly; and avoid cutting the nerve as far as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bloodletting from the cephalic [vein] helps so much that it takes away blood from the head and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is fitting to bleed at the olive or myrtle vein, for it is the most safe of all veins, because there is no nerve or artery below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is fitting to seek the lighter place, and do not harm anything if one must try again, and start over.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance some people's veins swell when one tries for the first time, but it does not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that it is not done except for preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid impending illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins that are cut: namely, the cephalic, the facial, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed in the beginning of primes, that is to say, when a person is young, and in autumn and winter after meals, when the sign of repletion appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should bleed either on the first or third day, after 2 or 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bloodletting that is administered for illnesses has no fixed determined time, but when need arises by day or night, in all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not fitting to bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman carrying more than four months' gestation until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should elderly people who have passed 60 years not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever way it may be, it is fitting that they first cleanse their bowels with a light enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has many phlegms retained, so that the veins do not remove from the intestines the superfluities which are harmful to the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should one bleed someone who is too full of meat, or who is drunk, until the excess has been purged away, nor those who are dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and beware of bleeding after colic passion, and vomiting, and purging of the belly, and frequent visits to a woman, and hard labor, watching late at night, and rising early, and all that pertains to bodily vigor, or by some wound or bodily hurt.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtlety the humors, if the blood is thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then enter or bathe, if nothing hinders it, to subtlety the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and take the blood from the vein around the third [ribs], as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day free of work, and strife, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be laid up and joyful, and let the bloodletting be higher than that which one is bleeding from, and stroke the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then stretch the ligament above moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then stroke the place with your hands, until the veins swell and can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the bloodletting place with a little old oil, and then put his thumb of his left hand on that vein below the place where he wants to bleed.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not break or burst when cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow like strings at the time of bleeding, and some that are full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when you put your thumb on the vein, it withdraws and cannot be opened, and thus one is among those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if the vein has opened too much, it is the wound too tight, therefore one should be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens at first time, that's good; but if not, then start again a little below or above that place in haste, unless the veins are swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the vein is swollen and the patient is frightened, let it rest for a day or two, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps an abscess will come forth; do not enter into bathing, then start again with bleeding if it pleases.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it will not flow as much as you see, then trust in that very opening for all the right blood flow.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work somewhat hastily, so that the parts are swollen; for it often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the part swollen, do not start stitching again, and put a little bit of oil on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and is good for this part, the oil that brings ease.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in each stitching that you close the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and it does the same thing in triple and double folds, when you put it on the part; so subtlety separates and spreads out when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not drained except at that time or the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hurry and put on the part a moist sponge in water and wine, slightly warm, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if some blackness or greenish color remains on the part for several days, it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on something of aloe or myrrh dissolved in camphor, poultice-like, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and swelling appear at the stitching of the basilica: then put your hand on it, and if you find the part soft to the pressure of your hand, that is a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything on it of what we have said, for by chance there may be a constriction in the artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the part, then care for it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each bloodletting according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it thin out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is full and strong, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and let the flaps be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and let him heal a little at a time, and have him healed by cutting across, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing is safe from the evacuation of blood and the compression of nerves, and is more effective than stitching the long or the wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to the one whose body is too weak for stitching, it is necessary to give a moist poultice made from grape juice; if he is overheated, let him bleed three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, before the stitching, give him a moist poultice in a honeyed syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-odored syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he vomits after the bleeding, after a good flow of blood, it is necessary that he drinks broth made from beef and a subtle, well-odored syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and follow the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to vent his arm and heal another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to vent his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he heals in seven hours after the first bleeding, or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wants to heal from another side, then he should heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is a great deal of blood inside the body that is already overheated and brings on fever; so it is necessary to let out a large quantity, and dilate the aperture as much as possible.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then that you fulfill all the conditions of healing, and put your hand on the parts when they heal, so that death may not come in place of convalescence.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this often happens when the surgeon is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not happen when you see the arm untied and the blood flowing out the second time, and the aperture is closed, unless you press firmly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if he is bent, let him straighten his arm quickly, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it stay until it heals the second time; or you should pierce to the tip of the flap, until the blood that is frozen at the opening of the vein issues forth.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on a little bit of wine soaked in water, and press down gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not bind it tightly, until the abscess is calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity demands the bleeding of blood the second time, then let him bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein within the arm is stitched instead of the head vein because it is compounded.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of stitching is that the patient dips their hand in hot water until the blister is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then let him heal across, not lengthwise or widthwise.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the aperture should be wide, and it should be stitched well near the joint of the hand, and if the blood cannot issue, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's in summer, then don't put the hand in hot water again, because one puts it more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the stitching of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The stitching of the wrist on the right hand is worth to all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and dip it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, so that one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the stitching is across, and you cut all around it, then nothing will hurt.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't go too far inward, because the nerves are underneath all these layers of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot issue.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let out the blood as far as necessary, then put oil and silk on the vein to cauterize it quickly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The surgery of the right hand is equal to the illness of the left mouse, and does the same as I told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The surgery of the Sophen [sciatic nerve] is equal to all diseases that are under the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as illnesses of the kidneys, and retention of urine, and disease of the loins, and old hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his surgery is that the patient puts their foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it bleeds.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and he presses above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot many urines go.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	he then opens up either a larger wound or one at the ankle that is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you make the incision on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are below, and make the incision also as when cutting; and let the flames be evenly placed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the bleeding fails at first, then start again the second time above a little bit, because the flesh is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	nor be afraid of nerves, as we have said, and thus do the same surgery on the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its surgery is worth the pain of the haunch when it's for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of his surgery is that the patient goes into a bath and stretches above the ankle four fingers while twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	because otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then cut it in all ways you can, and crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it's worth more than you cut it, because the flesh is salted, and it's very well received by many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't find it, then make an incision in any vein that opens at the back of the foot or towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make so much flow of blood as you see, and then loosen the ligament, and put on cotton and tighten it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	The surgery of the poultice
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Poultices are made of horns, or tin, or glass; and poulticing is done in two ways: either by wounding and attracting blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this poulticing that is done without wounding is done in two ways: either it is with heat, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and the poulticing that is done by wounding and extracting blood is done in 14 places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	from which one is all on the top of the head; and the others are inside the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in the two sides of the neck; and the poultice under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the poultice on the two shoulders; and the poultice above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the poultices in the two arms; and the poultices of the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the poultices of the two ankles; and the poulticing does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore one is not weakened by it, as with surgery of a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that she be administered, neither with heat nor without heat, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to poultice, or for habituations, then we administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they have need to poultice, then have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who find repletion and redness on their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen the tongue, and redden with blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who see visions, and behold by night blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order them to poultice after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The surgery of the mouth helps with the giddiness of the head... which comes to them, and it is not necessary that this be done after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this poulticing is in place of the surgery of the cerebral.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not necessary for someone who has a cold complexion to use it, or who has catarrh, because this would cause them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not necessary for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often cure themselves with it, then become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to put the poultice a little lower down because of the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The poulticing in the neck is in place of the surgery of the head and the brain, and therefore it is worth it for the constriction of the chest.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for breaking of the channel of the womb, and for all, and for repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to apply it a little more strongly, because if it holds too tightly, it will induce forgetfulness or obstruction of the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The poulticings on the two sides of the neck are worth it for the pains of the head, and obtalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and for the pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in place of the surgery of the brain; and it is necessary that you instruct the surgeon to extend their hand when applying, so that they do not cut the artery, and do not cause excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The poulticings under the chin are worth it for mouth diseases, and for the corruption of gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the surgeries of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The poulticings on the shoulders are worth it for the disease that comes from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The poulticings on the sides are worth as much as the three veins of the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it drains blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon not to cut too deeply in front, because the skin is thin and lies over nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the rump is worth to hemorrhoids of the foundation, and to diseases below, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large, and be made of earth, so that it may well draw out; and by chance, if they were subtle, they would break; and it would cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs so heal manifestly, for they draw out blood from all the body, and are worth to ancient pains of the kidneys, bladder, and urine, and restore flowers; and they are located on the two Sophene regions, and the two ankles, although they weaken the body after long use, and bring forth numbness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on the suction cup is that you first put it empty, and suck in a timely manner, and then place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the red and swollen area, and appear the redness of the blood; then cease, and remove the suction cups, and take heed to the condition of the body, for there are some who have hard flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and somewhat deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to subtlety the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out some little by little, we suffice only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to draw out a lot of blood, we repeat often; and if the blood is thick, we strike in deep, and the end is that the veins are pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for one who has thick skin and hard flesh, and who have large pores, that you anoint the places of the suction cups with oil that is appetizing and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, with purple oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, with oil of cress, or lily, or chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter oil, or balm oil, or oil of anise, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if one is cured with soft flesh and large pores, there is no need to put any oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or water of pear, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And one who has a lot of moisture, should get up with ease, or with water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should get up with old wine, or water of sycamore, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar ones.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and one does not need to be cured with a suction cup before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one does not sleep after the suction.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he washes himself when he should be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And take heed if one who is being cured is choleric, and the blood is too abundant and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as ripe grapes, and endive, and lettuce at ease, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and young pigeons, and kid's flesh, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And one who has a cold complexion, should take honey syrup, and moderately aromatic wine, which is between old and new, and young pigeons, and small birds, and partridges.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he will be suctioned, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or muscade before the suctioning, or after, to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be subtlety drawn out, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink this.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are placed without striking are those that are placed on the liver, and on the kidneys, and podagra, and on the belly and the bowels and the kidneys and the genitals, because those members do not endure being struck elsewhere.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does this only to draw blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as we put on the nipples when the child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, such as we put suction cups on the belly and on the bowels to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes pain when there is inflammation or abscess; and by its attractive virtue, it happens that the inflammation subsides, or dislodges the abscess from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and on the kidneys when there is retained suction.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these suction cups are administered empty in order to suck as much as possible; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with warm water only, or with water in which herbs suitable for this purpose have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered by fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two inches of width and half a palm in depth, and it has on the edge around the middle one small pit, just as to receive an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it is of earth, soft before use so that it does not hurt the patient when putting it on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and it has in the middle a bar of transverse earth or iron, to put a candle holder.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they are great and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups for children are different from those for old people, and for thin ones than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus put this suction cup on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candle holder of wax or one lining, and put it inside the suction cup across the bar that is inside the suction cup.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light may be at the bottom of the suction cup, so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and let the two ends be on the pit that we have said, so that when one wants to, the vapor goes out, and one removes the suction cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and one takes the lining again, just as before, and renews it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass then which is administered in the disease of pleurisy, at all ages, there is no rod nor puncture, and it is not applied except when it is full of water, and it is placed on the member so only.
et c’est li forme:	and it's like that:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Cups are not applied except in members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar parts;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare bones, such as toes or nails, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find cups that are in sweet and clear waters without perturbation, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put one in sweet water, as long as they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then let it be cleansed with wine and cupping glass, then rub the member until it is red, and put the cups on;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and burst, then if it is a place where one can put cupping glasses, he puts them, for this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then take the place away from air and then from water, well, and then stretch it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place is still sore after the cups' contact with the body, then soak one linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the cupping glass is contracted;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the cupping glass is multiplied, then put on crushed vitriol, or gall, and similar things, until it is contracted;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put half a handful of peeled fava beans on the place and leave them until they are cooked at the place, then it will be stanch now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other cups.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the cups don't want to be taken, then wipe the place with fresh blood or insert a needle until some blood flows,
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will be absorbed;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are bursting, then powder on a little bit of aloes and burnt silk or ashes, so they will burst now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a treatment for fracture and desolation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the foolish eye will not gaze upon this chapter, for they have never seen any of the old books nor read them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this, the art is estranged in our land, for I never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing about it, except by the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the art, and by experience, and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have abridged it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of instruments that are applied, just as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore fitting that we say the prologue to this book, which contains the summaries of words and chapters where wise men put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient from one part and another, unless something else entirely prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or young children, or the elderly.
