ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the weather is not very cold or too hot; and besides, cold humors are bad, that is to say, cold chills, and the flesh of hare and of goat, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any greasy foods, and do not fill oneself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about hot abscess or spreading of matter in the member; then revive the patient under their former government which they had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or if they have viscosity, such as boiled wheat in water, and rice, and testicles, and peas, and pork belly, and eel, and fresh fish, and rich wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with great nourishment the bones are restored more quickly and the fracture is healed sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old men and those who are decrepit cannot be well restored or united according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as children's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but take no care, reset the broken bone with one big splint that sets and joins the member together, until it is as strong as before; and do not cease from your work, and for this reason you must nourish with rich meats, just as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is one thing and the fracture of the belly or leg is another, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur by being struck, and others by being crushed, such as the cutting of a feather to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And then there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture in a small split or crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own design, and proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings forth in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the fracture of the bone is by twisting the place, and it becomes apparent by deviation, and sounds under the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or crunching, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may well have a twist, or split, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you must not move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come next, and then gently restrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fractures that occur by being struck, and are the two parts separated, it is necessary to put them back together in equal points, lest hot abscesses come into being.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if hot abscesses come into being, then leave it alone for a day, until the abscess is appeased;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it back together in equal parts as you can do lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of one bone is easier than the restorations of those who have pieces; then restrain it, just as it should be done next.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, and it is stretched to two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or at your hand if it is small members, or to two cords, or to one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, then reset by all means the addictions in their places as much as you can, and take care that through your work there is no injury or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join well the two joints of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well: so straighten it nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press it as those who cause by their work abscessed heat and contraction in the member, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is set, then chastise well the patient so that he does not move it, nor in waking nor in sleeping, nor in turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, then it is not in place, and it must be put in such a disposition that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is set correctly, so that there may not come twisting when he is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken member are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar: so it is necessary to envelop them in cloths of soft and subtle linen.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and leg: so it is necessary to envelop them in a wide and sturdy bandage, for the broad bandages encompass all the great member, and restrain it evenly from all parts, so that there may be no crevice.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around light cloths, three turns or four according to the member, and strain your hand a little on all the bandage, then go above the break and restrain it less, so that the break may shift slightly away from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage a little and a little, until you take up a great part of the healthy flesh, then take another bandage, and wrap it around again above the broken bone.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break, and restrain it moderately, not too strongly nor too gently, as we have said in the first lesson above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the bandages cloths of linen or drapes, as long as it is all equal, then tie everything above one binding, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, then put on something soothing to the abscess hot, and which removes the swelling, and let it be thus for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then set upon your splints, and be made of half a well-cured cane, or of fir from which one makes cleaves, or of palm bark, and be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint which one puts on the break is a little larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it is needed for the member of smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then set upon the splints as you did in the first lesson, then tie above with a thread in a way, as in the first lesson on the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the tighter it is above, the looser below; and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, like I have seen in the works of fools who do their bandages with cords of linen twisted in a knot, and that is great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it does not need to have less than two fingers' width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the splints after the straining in their healthy parts, then put under them cloths of linen or felted wool, so that he does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breakage, and the ligaments are broken, I will speak of its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to set splints on all the broken members the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it is not necessary to put splints on them until after five or six days, or more according to your security against abscesses happening.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and see here the manner of ancient plasters to restore breakage, dislocation, and twisting: and it is that you take flour that remains at the sides of the mill, and mix it with a great many eggs, and put this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the breakage in various conditions, and indeed for women and small children, for it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting: take aloes and ladani and inula and assefeitide and gum arabic and mugat, each 10; myrrh and aloe, each 5; alechil 8; and make powder, and mix it with many eggs; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is valuable to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is good for twisting: take mugat and vismalve, each 10; myrrh and aloe, each 8; acaice 6; Armenian bolic 10, and grind well, and mix it with water or many eggs, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of plaster for joints and bones that are separated from their places, and soothes the pain that follows, and the use of the bone, and the breakage: take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and hot oil, and put it on the place. These plasters do not restore, but they are good for soothing abscesses hot, and remove properly the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried leaves of fig tree and leaves of terrestrial papyrus, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of bone breakage and to soften the remaining abscess. Take root of vismalve, camomile, violet flowers, farina of vetch, each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the member is inflamed, mix with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another way to plaster more strongly than the first one, when an abscess persists to the restoration of the member. Take roots of vervain, and seeds of flax, balsam, melilot, and sassafras, and flowers of violets and chamomile, from each take a part; and grind, and mix with saltwater, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the warmth of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that one should not put on the broken member to restore it with a cerot made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says that it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken member to restore it with things dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster that is good for a lesion and pain: take mugwort and horsehair of sheared men or bird feathers, and vervain, in equal parts, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then remove the plaster a little later, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor does their bone move out of its place; if not, do not remove it by hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, you hasten and remove it, and take off the plaster now; and take light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and plunge into water, and lift up the area, until the itching ceases, and the pain is alleviated.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it with a knot, until you are sure of warm abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation of the member rest, and let the pain be removed, then start again with gentle binding, and a little plaster, and do not strain it so hard as before; and bind gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is gone and red and painful and swollen are all removed from it, and you need to plaster and bind, then start again in the same way as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if none of what we have said comes to the member, then do not remove it until after three days or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what is seen, until the broken part is set and approaches the bone's contact with it.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then restrain it more than before, and let the flesh grow its own fat, as I said before; and if you see the area drying out more than is necessary, know that no nourishment can come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then rise the member with warm water twice a day, every time you remove it, and gently loosen the binding.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this work then cut off the nourishment to the member, and hasten what fools do, that leave the member twisted: it is bad, and it is a laborious and woeful thing, and I see nothing else but languor and right working.
des diverses manieres de brisure	The various ways of breaking [injuries]
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many kinds of breakages and diverse forms, and the causes are assigned.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are breakages that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the arm takes away all the bone down to the sacrum which is below the bone, as does a hatchet or a club; and for this reason it is called "hachuring".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above without piercing, and is called this kind of breakage "absolute"; and the wound from these two breakages is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is an embedded percussion, or a splitting, or a blow from the fist of stone, or from falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is a persistent breakage which approaches just to the membrane that is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is reunited in the bone as fine as a hair, and it is a small splitting, and for this reason it is called this breakage "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and causes the bone piece to go down, and it is like the holes that blacksmiths make when they hammer on the cauldrons; then the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have or had moist bones, like the heads of infants.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens to all these kinds of breakages where small pieces are torn off, as they are; and I will speak of this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of breakages by their subtraction above them, and the inquiry into their tents, and through the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by this, that when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed it gently above, then opens up the black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the breakage, take care to note the accidents of the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of blood, loss of intellect, swelling, palpitation, fever ague, and the flesh issuing forth and turning red, and other similar things in many dispositions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unbearable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the 14th day at the latest that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the 7th day, so that the membrane below the bone is corrupted, and come the accidents that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the breakage of the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you split the split part thus: and this is that you take hold of the wounded patient's head, and uncover above the bone in all ways that you can, and above the shape of the wound as gently as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if bleeding comes to uncover the bone or abscess appears hot, then provide what is needed, and this is that you fill the area with damp cloths in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed and you are assured of no more bleeding; then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you cut at the narrow cutting before, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another shape larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have diverse shapes, some being narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of untempered iron; and work lightly, lest you wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and rough, then you must pierce around it, so that you give shapes with rasps, not too deep lest they go beyond the bone of the skull, and it should have above the point a margin or one circle, so that the point does not go beyond the bone; and you need to have several, so that each becomes its place in the shape of the bone, so that you have rasps for all tests; and this is the form of the three manners of rasps:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one rasp on the bone and turn it in your hands until you know the bone has been pierced; then place the rasp elsewhere a little further, and do this all around, then file away the incisors of the bone which is between the ridges, and make it more subtly than you can, lightly, as we have said, so that you bring the bone to your hand or to one of your tools like pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you rasp off the roughness that remains on the bone to all one another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be more tempered and subtler than the other incisor;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if there remains nothing of the small bones or scales, then remove them lightly with one of your instruments; then care for the wound with poultices and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which the Gauls say, which is more sound; and they love it very much, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lenticular incisor, and this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and the piece is laid in two parts, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer on top, so that you file lightly all around the bone, and take good care of the skin that is beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is stuck to the bone, then file lightly, for one files well without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate to the skin, and the bone is filed away only on top, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that roughness, and to remove scales with a subtle scraper which you should have in various quantities, so as to administer in each place what is most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	So start with large scrapers, and then move on to more subtle ones, and do not stop until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-like and subtle breakages, it is necessary that you administer according to its direction; and this is something that is not known to him who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the spine is uncovered, then it is necessary that you take one linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another doubled cloth in two or three layers, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not injure the spine, then administer above one more layer of linen, and do not stretch it too much as long as it covers only the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it thus for one or two days until the abscess is appeased, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristology, and similar things; and make powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and administer medicines again without mordication.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and take care that the wound is soon clean, so that you do not leave any ointment there, nor let it assemble bowels, for when bowels assemble on the skin of the brain, they will corrode and burst forth, and bring great harm to the patient; for when something mordant is put on the spine, it will necrotize above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore take care then, if any bad accidents befall the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if there is no further evil that comes from the medicine you have put on, but it has such virtue, then it is necessary that you take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and glue one cloth, and place it on the spine;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the treatment in ways that are necessary until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the neck above are broken, or one on its own, because these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you put your small finger or perturbation into the neck, and place this breakage inside your index finger and at the back, as long as the neck returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and take care that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the neck and cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you put it equal at the head of a rod slightly large.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then do it likewise, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess is appeased, then put a cloth on the head of the neck, with linen cloths, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you put another on the other side, if there is a break there; and let the tents be so large that they fill the perturbations of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorers say that the tents should be moistened with butter and changed each day. It does not seem to me that this is well, but it is necessary that they be moistened in a concoction of egg whites, and mill powder; then leave the tent until the bone is hard and the cartilage is toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one places a bottle or eggshell instead of tents, and if it has a single soft draping around, and holds the breeze, and blows on the patient among them; or does what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess forms nearby while you are working there, then put a poultice or damp cotton cloth in oil of rosins, or in one pot of aquilone.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess does not form, then put an embrocation by the door, of barley meal and powder of incense, mixed with egg white, then put it on light steaming, and do not bind the nearby area.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break of the near area is small, and it is broken into little pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments for that, then sew the wound, and care for things that are rough, hard, or swelling, as suitable plasters and unguents are.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the near area, then care for tents, and put linseed seeds in it, until he is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken below, and there is no wound outside, and the break is just so, and is not split in two, only that it is known slightly inside, one recognizes it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part of the jawbone, that you put your two index fingers in the mouth of the patient; and if the break is in the left side of the mandible, then put your two index fingers from the right hand, and press the break slightly inside, and bind it with equal force.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is split in two, then it is necessary that you administer an extension of three parts, until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movements of the teeth occur, or fracture, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put a poultice on the broken jawbone, and put a double drapery on it; and put a great iron plate, well made, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, and bind it as tight as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and give him light victuals.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the shape is changing, then loosen it on the third day, and then put back what has changed; and put a poultice on it, of mill powder with egg white or barley meal, after you have removed the previous poultice; and put a light woolen cloth on top, and if the poultices harden, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it so until he is healed; many times he is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess forms, then apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, take care that no part of the bone is left; if subtlety to extract with suitable instruments for that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none left, then sew the wound if it is large, and put suitable poultices on top to bring forth flesh, until he is healed.
de la forcele	of the fracture
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture is broken multiple times in front of the shoulder, and the break is such that it is divided into three manners: or it is broken and split in two, with pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such when the break has no wound that you have two assistants, so one holds the assistant's tool that feels the fractured forcele; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then put the break in your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor unevenness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, then place under the shoulder of the patient a rounded spear of cloth or wool, and make it thick according to your need; and strain and lift the forcele, and hold the spear in your hand, so that you put the break in its proper position.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forcele forward because it comes from behind, then it is necessary that the patient lies sovining on his hatedil, and puts a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder; and instructs the assistants to bring down the shoulder, until the bone of the forcele is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your hands, and if you find it disjointed, then it is necessary that you split it open; and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, then file it with one of the incisors that you have; but put this instrument under the forcele to protect the sac.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and resembles a spoon, and is not uneven, and be as large as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two handles, just as you see, and one handle be wide, and the other handle be narrow, just as is the fracture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of a hot abscess, then sew the wound, and if the fracture is small, or you doubt it may be a hot abscess, then pack the wound with cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, then soak a cloth in oil of rosins, and vinegar, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The treatment of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put a poultice on the bone made of mill powder and egg white, and put light steam on top, and put a spear under the armpit, if you need to.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide band of palm leaves, about 3 fingers in width and length, and wrap it around the poultice and steam; then take a fine plate of 3 fingers in width and length, and enwrap it around that band, so that the head of the band is pendant.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the plate on top of the break, and turn the band around the neck, and under the armpit healthy, and under the armpit sick; and straighten each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the break well, and you clearly see that the plate does not move above the broken bone, then rewrap it each day, and when the ligaments relax, restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos,
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, and let it be restored thus, until it is restored; and it is restored in the most at .xxviij. days, and in less to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It often happens that the shoulder breaks or becomes loose, and it does not seem to be inflamed except by touch; so one should dress according to the figure of the break, and reset according to its natural form, in all ways you can; then put powder from the mill with a great deal of egg white on the joint, and light bandages, and put on 1 double cloth; then put on a wide and subtle bandage, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there are any threads under the bandage anywhere on the shoulder, take that thread of linen, so that the bandage stays evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large strap, so that the bandage does not move from its place, and watch over each day; and every time it swells, bind it again, and put the bandage back in its place if it gets out of joint, and let the patient sit on his side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25. And when this number is completed, then release it, and be sure, for it is not bone that becomes inflamed lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes before and points under the skin, then fill it with, and remove the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the humerus to calm down an inflamed abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the rib
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The rib is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it breaks often at the end. And when it is broken inside, it inclines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks air, and all, and by chance vomits blood, and opens up the cracks in the broken bone, and one senses it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient sits up on his back, and puts 1 cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of the two sides with your hands, and makes it even in all ways you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then put emplaustres and bandages above the subtle bandage of salt, or another light one, and wraps it in 1 cloth, and ties it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the binding back around to the back, and bind it gently, and reward each hour by loosening, and if it swells again, bind it again; and if it is necessary to unbind due to corrosion or pruritus that comes at the joint, or pain or abscess, then hasten and unbind, and remove the emplaustre, and address what has come forth in ways of cures; then reset the emplaustre, and bind it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not come forth except in thick places after the back, and at the top inside, and do not bend forth except because they are slippery; and one senses it well by probing the back.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you put the break even as it should be. And then put an emplaustre and bind with a bandage if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is declining inwardly, then the patient feels extremely great pain and piercing, as if from pleurisy, for the bone pierces the skin; and breathes with difficulty, and all, and vomits a great amount of blood, and this is grievous sickness, and the ancients have placed great importance on it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly to push the breakage away from the inside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, unless an inflamed abscess has come before it.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that one should put poultices on the joint to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the poultice might attract unnecessary substances to the joint due to the condition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us say that one should cover the joint with moist wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make even the breath around, then take care of the treatment for pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure through the bone that pierces the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut open above the joint of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to keep the syphac from happening; and then one must cut the bone, and pull it lightly, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and cure with emplaustres until he is healed. And if inflamed abscesses come, then put wet cloths in rose oil on top of the joint; and cure the joint for as long as necessary to treat the abscess, and be cautious as you can sit on the side where it should be, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Rarely does the breakage come to the bone of the neck, and it does not often bend forth; and similarly with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you see that he will not be healed or not, then take heed if you see his hands softening and swelling and dead, and cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, it does not feel. Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they become numb and feel well when one tightens and pricks them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient is cured, if one puts care into it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you see that he will not be healed or not, then take heed if the feet are softened, and if there is a swelling on the hands, and on top of the back there is windiness and evacuation without will; and when one has soothed him on his stomach, there is evacuation without will. And when he is soothed on his back and wants to belch, but cannot. Know that it is mortal: if one does not labor in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then the thing is more easy.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you reward him if there is an inflamed abscess, by putting rose oil or egg yolk oil on top of the spine, until he is calmed; then put a soothing and drying emplaustre on it, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Et if some bone is severed, so cover on the wound; and take away the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is great, with a suture, then anoint with ointment, extracting flesh, until it is healed; and if the skull of the bone is broken, which is called the "bone of the cow", so put your pouch in your left hand, and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then put the poultice and plaster on, if you need it; then strain it, and if there is a severed bone, do that, and take away the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the breaking of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does, there follows a little diminution at the head; and do long and decline by degrees, and comes to the patient in pain at the spot, and punctures, and swells up what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand above, until you are above the breakage; and know what kind of breakage it is and its shape; and if the breakage is only at the head, so set equal to that breakage, until it is in natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is of the length, or it declines inwardly, so make the patient lie on their belly, until the restoration of that breakage appears to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it equal, so put on the poultice, then put on a plaster of wood or horn, and hold the breakage still, so that it does not move; and apply the place below the ribs, until the sides are equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess forms there, do not touch it, until the abscess is calmed down, and put on what we have said before; then come back to the restoration, and hold it still as is necessary, if there is no bad accident; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires is that which is between the shoulder and the head of the arm, and if it is broken, then it must be restored according to one of the two manners: one of which is that you take one piece of plain wood, about the size of this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two strings, and bend them up high, and make the patient sit on one chair; then throw their broken arm onto the wood, until it comes to the desired position, and has about half a covering of wood, then bend it over some heavy thing or let the attendants stretch it down below; then put the mallet on the breakage equal to your hands together, until the breakage returns as is necessary.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that you make the patient sit on their haunches, and tie their hand to their neck; then instruct two attendants to have one hold what is above the breakage in their hands, and the other hold below all one string, and stretch each one to his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then hold one string below the breakage and above the breakage, and have each attendant stretch to his part. And if the breakage is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put one string in the middle under the seat, and another towards the arm pit, under the breakage; and similarly if the breakage is towards the arm pit, there is a need to put one string lightly, without labor, until the breakage is equal on both the head and the arm pit; then set the breakage equal as necessary, and hold it, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess forms there, do not hold it at all for seven days, and put on a moist poultice in a warm place and with rose oil, until the abscess is calmed down; then hold it, and the manner of holding it is that you put the poultice on the breakage, then bring the arm onto the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put the bandage, and hold it on the shoulder and arm, so that the arm is in a steady state, unless something hinders it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use plasters, and put on the breakage a larger and stronger plaster than the others, with about two inches of space between each one, and so that each plaster is as large as it passes over the breakage three inches from each side; then hold on to the plasters, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the breakage, stronger and less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the setting of the plasters and the binding, just as we said, in the work that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is hot, let it be left to bind for seven days, just as we said; then look at each three days the bandage, that itching or swelling does not come to the place, or numbness cannot come to the member because it is too tight. If this happens, do as we said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents come, do not remove the bandage for more than three days or so, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach; and put a cushion made of linen under the shoulder equally, and look at each hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken member does not change, or the bonds do not loosen; if it is directed by the virtue of medicine, and give the food we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is for the first subtleties; and when it begins to recover, let it be thick. And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be recovered in forty days entirely; and then one must remove the bandage and administer baths and medicines of ointments to direct the place. And if the constriction is ugly and swollen, one should wait until it is removed for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", of which one is small, and that is the one that supports the pouch; and the other is large, and that is the one that is below, towards the little finger. By chance, break only the large foscile alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small fosciles are broken, the restoration is easy and healing; and when the large one is broken, then the healing is bad, and more painful than when both are broken together. If it's the small foscile that's broken alone, it should be slightly extended and made equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the great fissure, then it must be strained more strongly; and extend on one cushion, and hold the pouchet of the hand higher than the others, and the little fingers lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross-legged in front of himself, so that he does not suffer any labor; then extend the attendants' arms to the part below his hand, or to a strap, and another attendant to one above. And then place the patient evenly, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has fragments, then place each one in its place, and if there is any fragment that holds the key, and you cannot restore it to its place, then proceed with force and osteum, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken of it in a single chapter; then take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the setting right there come abscesses, then make a poultice made of rose oil and white wax, that it is neither too hard nor too soft; and tie the poultice on top subtly, until the abscesses are calmed. Then remove the poultice, and put in the plaster of mill powder with abundant egg yolk, then place the stitches, and let the stitch be of the break more strong, and a little wider than the others; and know that it should have 7 stitches or arms in multiple dispositions: whether the break is in one bone or two; and strain more on the break than elsewhere, and always less in advancing, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the drapes that are above the break be soft and moist, and not hard nor harsh; and let the thread, with which it is strained, be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And reward the member and the strap after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some bad accident happens to the member, such as pruritus which comes to the member, then it is necessary that you bathe the member with hot water, until those pruritus are calmed; and let the member not at all rest tightly.
