And then resume the straining, and if the strap is worn out and the bone dislocated, and similar things, then address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then it is necessary that you soften it a little bit, and let it be thus for some days, until the swelling comes, and then strain.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not loosen it until 20 days or so, then bind his hands to his neck, and let his necks be even, and beware of movement and contortion, and sleep on his back; and know that this break is restored in 30 days or so, and by chance in 25 days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	(None)
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and among the fingers, there are many breakages, and but few abscesses come.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the finger of the hand is broken or bent, then it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged and sit straight in front of him evenly; then place his hand on the extended cloth, and extend the attendants' fingers, and set them even with the mire, until they are well joined; and put a plaster and poultices, if abscesses do not come, then put a stitch according to the quality of the linen; and be wrapped in one poultice of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is around the knuckle of the finger, then make a sphere of drapes, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken finger; and then strain with a long drape, and let the stitch be as soft as the flesh of the hand, and strain, as it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the end, then it is necessary that you put a stitch on top, and another one below in the finger, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind everything around the hand, and stop the strap between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of our fingers, except for the thumb, then set it even, as is necessary; and bind with the finger, and see if you put a straight small stitch to lift the break, and does not move; and if the break is in other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, then set it even, and bind with the healthy finger that comes after; or you bind them all together, just holding what's worth it, or you put a stitch on top, like on the thumb; and take care in the restoration and disposition of abscesses hot, and address what comes, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	(None)
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the ankle is often broken, and one can see when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that you tie one strap above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each attendant stretches his strap to his part evenly; and that is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is close to the root of the ankle, then one of the straps goes towards the elbow, and the other strap below the break. And also if it is close to the knee, and then the strap is placed below the knee, and the extension is downward; then put the mire on the bone evenly with both hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then put a plaster, and bind, if abscesses hot do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess hot, then let it be calmed and then return to your work and your care; the binding is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the break with a bandage of double thickness in two or three layers, and remove any superfluous parts; then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the knee, and put a long thread between the ankle and the leg, below the knee, and let the ends of the thread come up; then turn the bandage over the leg and ankle, then put stitches on the break, and put one stitch above the bone of the leg; then apply the leech between the leg and ankle with soft drapes to equalize the binding, then begin to bind firmly in three or four turns around the break; and as you go higher up the break, and less you strain; then attend to the two ends of the thread that you have put between the leg and ankle, and tie three stitches that are above, then return down to the bottom of the thread, until you come to the foot; and bind, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, unless there comes an abscess or swelling or any other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is, then dislodge it and set straight what comes forth, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that pinch, then one must split it open, if possible; and if not, then one must cut through the ligament, and pull forward; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And any time the case is broken, one puts in splints, as in an arm or leg; nonetheless, in this restoration made it does not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the case is restored in one day, or perhaps less or more, according to the diversity of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the hollow of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the hollow of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, then it's just a split or a perforation, and it has to be treated for every wound, and without a wound, and this one knows well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one sets equal those things which are torn to their joints, as long as it can be assembled; then put an ointment, and put in a rounded splint, if you need it, and strain it as it should be, then reward all the dispositions we have said for other breaks, just like aposteme heat and similar things; and put what is needed to each accident, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "malleolus" and the other "fibula"; and it has all the same breakage as it comes to the arm, and therefore the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is all done.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the thick bone is broken, then one feels great pain and sees it well; and it turns below. Then apply an extension, and set it equal, and tie the splints evenly; but nonetheless, it's necessary if the break is ugly and there are more pieces, that the extension be smaller and lighter; and adjust according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two pieces of split wood that correspond to the length of the leg from one end to the other, and wrap them around the leg with bandages on top and bottom, and tie it in the middle as well; and so the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and some people wrap a wooden splint along the length of the leg, and it is made of wood, and one puts the leg to prevent movement, and properly does what is needed for the break or wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is aposteme heat or another accident; and cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no breakage, but sometimes the bones of the foot do break and the toes are a little bent, and it's nothing more than some slight movement.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot break and you see those bones overlapping each other, then set the patient's foot on the ground, as if it were going to walk; and then put your own foot on top of his, at the place where the bones are lifted up; then press down so they return to their places; then apply an ointment and cover with a cloth on top, and put underneath the belly of the foot a small tablet with two full cheeks; then tighten it to the foot accordingly; and when you have wrapped bandages around, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days will have passed, then loosen the binding, for you will find the bones equalized, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are some broken toes, then restore them, as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then put on each broken toe a splint according to its length, and make it slightly wider, then place underneath the foot that tablet which I mentioned, and strain it accordingly; and if there are three or four or more broken toes, then put a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and strain the tablet underneath the foot; and let it be so that the ventral part of the foot is held firmly.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it's necessary that you not forget the other things I have said about other breaks, as we have said; and treat each accident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the thumb bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the natural bone of a woman is broken, make her sit with legs apart, then bend her towards the back part, and hold her steady from behind; then fill the opening with cotton, and put in as big as one stone; then lift the woman up, and slowly lift the back part, and then the cotton will jump out until it reaches the entrance of the natural bone, and returns the bone with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, take away the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back on, and do this for seven days or so: then the break will be restored, and if you see that it is, take a bladder of herbs, and tie a string around the perforation, and pour all the bladder into the natural opening; then blow into the string strongly until the bladder is emptied inside: the natural bone will return to its place; then fill with cotton, and leave it like this for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the thumb bone of a man or woman is broken, restore it in the same way as we have said for the hip bone; and these nearby breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and practice into it, and intends to read my book. For the break indicates the right path of restoration in many dispositions: then heed this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gizzard and pour it into the penis; then wrap bandages around it, and let it be for three days or so, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaks with wounds
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with a wound, even if it is great, such as the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, and the wounds that we have said testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then keep it moist with vinegar, if you have nothing else; then begin again to restore the break in that same hour or day, lest apostemes come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess forms there, then let the restoration wait until the ninth day, so that the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing above the skin's surface, then it is necessary that you set it slightly to your hands, at a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not suited to set equal with your hands, then reamend this instrument made of iron, which has 8 or 9 inches length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for that reason it is necessary for the surgeon to take 3 or 4, according to what he needs in each breaking treatment; and be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend much under compression on the limb at your work, and be sharp before, and thick from halfway forward thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason it is necessary that the curved bone be placed on top of the apparent bone; and tie it once, until it recovers, and be equal one against the other. And if the breakage is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you trim the top of the bone, until the instruments have possession.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, or chisel or saw, to your ability; then ream out what remains in the bone of roughness and small scraps.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. So do as much as necessary to put it back in its place, then soak one cloth in black stiptic wine, and properly dress it; and do not put anything on the wound except oil until you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and trim the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the breakage; and many times this has been done by foolish surgeons, and they have brought suffering or death or corruption upon the patient at times; and the bandages should be softer and more gentle than those for other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that evil events may occur, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then it is not necessary to put on bandages; but wrap around, instead of bandages, hard cloths, and tie them. And when you see after one or two days a bow-like shape forming on the wound, then remove what you have placed on top with all wine, and apply ointment for healing wounds, such as ointment tetrafarmac and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb two times a day, morning and evening, until it is bound up and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be arranged in such a way that the bow-like shape runs down slowly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it cannot heal but instead returns to being bowed, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which reason it is necessary that you cleanse the wound with a tent, and remove all these devitalized pieces that bring about that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes to the site, or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is written in its chapter before this. And when the bone is broken and appears on the limb, such as the bones of the hip or shoulder, and other similar ones from the great limbs, do not remove it, for many times death comes, but let it be until it has purged; by chance it will come out after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come on the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see this after the healing of a break, especially when it is near the jointure, and it is a sad thing to behold the shape of the limb; and by chance the limb cannot perform its natural actions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if we are fresh: administer stiptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, acaica, and similar others, in such a way that you take some of these things or all together, and mix them with black wine or with abundant urine or with oil; and put it on the boil at night in cauldrons, and strain it well, and do not remove it for several days; then remove it, and begin another one, until the swelling is gone; or you can bind it with a piece of cloth well made; for the properties of cloth are such that they remove all swellings from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then cut it away, and make the superfluity apparent; or have it done by any razor, until it is removed, and cure it as long as it remains unhealed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone break is restored and the limb remains weak and subtle afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and could not allow the nourishment to reach the limb; or because of excessive swelling; or because of great movements, but not at its proper time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and give their body nourishment until the blood is multiplied in them; and administer baths to them, and give them joy and ease; then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and the swelling often subsides with warm water, until the nourishment flows to the limb; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bone appears, and the shape of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those foolish people who say that one must break the limb all over again; many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and great evils come from it, and by chance death itself; however, if the nodulations and tortures are fresh, then it is necessary to rise them with warm water, or cook soft herbs such as vervain leaves, roots, and melilotus, and similar things; and make a mollifying plaster, such as one made with dyaquilon well done, and take the mucilage of vervain and mix it with goose fat or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or take figs that are fatty, and grind them with flax seed, and similar medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by constant and continuous friction with moist hands. And it should be massaged gently every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is inflamed and hardened like stone, and it needs to be cut with iron, then it must be covered just to the bone, slightly incising finely; and put sense and study into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	There is no sentence to translate in this case, as "Ci encomence li livres des dislocations" appears to be the title or heading of a section within the text, rather than a sentence to be translated.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, then one must immediately restore it.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the swelling increases, and by chance, if one puts pressure on the swelling; therefore it is not good to move it until it has subsided: many times this brings on shame and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	However, when this happens, one should cause the patient to be healed, then leave it alone, until the swelling has been alleviated; then arise the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as the treatment comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It often happens that the jawbones are dislocated downwards, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: or they are slightly removed from their place, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot be held, nor can he close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in a few positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must immediately reset it, and do not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in such a way that the attendants hold the head of the patient, and place the mirror's pouch from one of their hands at the root of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-thirds; and the other two hands be free, to make equal; and instruct the patient to relax his jawbones, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror places it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to return, even if they are the two jawbones together, then raise them with warm water and oil, until you gently reset them; nor delay in returning, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well with some softening, then place wet cloths on it, made of rose oil and wax, and tie it gently with moist ligatures.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient sleeps on his back, and his joints being between two cushions, so that he does not move or strain to the right or left, nor does he exert himself to eat much, but takes light food, until the pains are removed, and the jawbones are relaxed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then moderate what he eats lightly, and does not trouble himself to open his mouth to eat and drink, until the jawbone is well relaxed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be returned to their place within an hour, and are not converted back to their position, then fever and usual habit come to pass, and by chance, solution of the belly, and by chance, vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a sign of death; and often the person who has it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the shoulder
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot dislocate from the front into its continuity and towards the chest, and is dislocated at times to the back, and it is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies sovain on his back, and stretches out his arms; then presses the dislocated place firmly against your palm, and it will return; then apply the ointment and bind it tight.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the bone that is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate; if not, and if it does dislocate at times, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the ointment and bind it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and similarly is reset the bone of the spine, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one of which is that it dislocates at the part below the armpit; and the second is at the part towards the chest; and by chance it dislocates at the upper part, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times dislocates below towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, because then it jumps forth quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps with a thud, and returns with a thud.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that there is a blow or crushing, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it has dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you inspect it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that the dislocation occurs when it goes down towards the armpit, and makes a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them a manifest diversity.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and below the armpit towards the toucher the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an os; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the toucher.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation is not other than to be reset when it is new or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the attendants lift the patient's hand up high, then place their fingers below the armpit, and lift the jointure with force to its place; and the attendants lift the hand, and stretch it out high, then put it back down; so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it doesn't come as we said within three days after, then it's necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and the attendant should use gentle and soothing remedies, such as a decoction of alecost, fenugreek, and melilotus in water, and apply them.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then instruct the patient to sit on their back, and place underneath the pillow a sheet of wool equal in thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the mirror under the patient's heel on the sheet, and lift the shoulder joint correctly, and guide the patient's hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another assistant holds the patient's head, so that it does not move downward; now the shoulder comes back to its place, and if you see that it is reset in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and that you make sure there is a person present, one who is greater than the patient; and be standing on the side, and push the shoulder under the pillow of the patient, and lift the pillow high, so that the patient hangs in the air.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another assistant guides the patient's hand downward towards their belly. And if the patient is too light, then let him carry something heavy with him, and the dislocation will come back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And reset it also in another way: and that is, to stick one long iron rod into the ground, so that its head is as level as a piston, and neither too big nor too small.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then place it under the patient, but so that there is a soft cloth above, and the patient's arm be extended downward from the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return by all these things we have said, then do this treatment: take one iron rod two arms thick and three fists wide, which has the head rounded so that it can enter easily into the depth under the pillow, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie it on top of the wooden beam with a soft cloth, so that the wood does not hurt the patient, then place it under the pillow of the patient; and stretch your arm over the long rod, and tie the assistant on top of the rod, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on one shoulder of an easel wide, and let the hands hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done, in whatever way it may be, then it is necessary that you place under the pillow a sphere of equal wool, then put the poultice wrapped with powder from the mill, with incense and an egg yolk, on all the shoulder and around, then strain the poultice under the pillow comfortably, and turn the cloth over the poultice, and enfold the hand in its own neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he rest a little, until the members are comforted, for he will heal more quickly; and then let him rest again after five days or seven, and move him; and if he is firm and has not been softened, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come in, or for another reason, then it is necessary that you administer cauterizations at three points, as described before in the chapter on cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and after seven days he still does not hold, and the joint will not lift his arm up, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is near the chest or breast or behind, is caused by impulse and stretching of hands, and another method is administered; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes swelling in the member and tardiness of movement, then have the patient take many baths until that swelling is alleviated, and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint is displaced at points, and returns at points; and if it is displaced from all sides, and especially before and behind, and the dislocation is not corrected, for one can see it well and feel it well; and displace according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the diseased shoulder with the healthy one, then it can be seen clearly. For the joint is deformed, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that the abscesses do not come to life again, for if the abscesses were to form again, it would be grievous to reset; and by chance it cannot be fully reset from all sides, especially when it is behind; so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance it brings death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such when it can be reset that you stretch his hand to your two hands; and his arms should be spread out, and his hands of the mirror according to the shoulder around, above, and below, and push the joint to its crevices together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and pushes the shoulder which is displaced from its place at the root of the palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, then administer strong extension; and have two ministers extend the arm, and hold it in place with their hands, so that it does not move at all from the extension; then turn the arm of each side, after you have wrapped a double-layered cloth long and wide.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the nurse has joined the joint to her hand, she anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then pushes the joint gently, until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is at its place, then put on a poultice with egg yolk and hold it gently, and bend the arm to the neck of the patient, and let him rest for some days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the bandage and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the poultice and the bandage, and let it be thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels swelling after the setting of the joint, and it becomes inflamed, then bathe him and gently rub him, and press until it is alleviated; or you put a sheep's fat snow on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make it enter into the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	and when he sweats, then gently rub the joint, then put the snow back on, and then enter into the bath; and thus do it two or three times, until he is healed; and if you see, then put hay of moist vetch warmed with butter, and hold it there; and it will return to its natural state.
li dislocation de la main	Hand dislocation
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The jointure of the hand dislocated, and the return is light, more than the other joints Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place promptly, in the same time that it is dislocated, so long as the swelling remains or an abscess forms hotly.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the return is that you place the ailing hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of the hand, and the fingers put it even, so that it places its palm on the appearance of the joint, and hold it until it recovers.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Nevertheless, you should look to see if it is well in place; then have the patient put the back of his hand on a table for stretching and returning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then have the patient put the back of his hand on the table, and the fingers put their hand on that appearance of the joint. If it returns now, it is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then strain ointments soothing abscesses hotly, and leave it thus without recurring.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it in place after some days, the joint remains twisted;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and nothing is worse for the patient than until the hand is softened, and he cannot strain any thing at all: then know that the nerves are strained, or the arteries; so there is no other remedy worse than to strain by fire cautery in this case, and perhaps it is not worth anything.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the ointment that we have said, then strain and leave it five days, then release and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any stiffness, then soak the water hot, and rub it until he is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	At times the fingers of the hand are dislocated at each part, sometimes at the back of the palm or in the wrist;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then the fingers are straightened, and hold the dislocation in your hands until it recovers, then support the tip of the finger, and guide it towards the part where it is separated;
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and leave it for two days, then put it even on that day; and tie the nut, as we have said, and release it from day to day, and make it move, and tie the nut again; and do this often until it is straight.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same thing if it is dislocated in the wrist of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same thing when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the hip of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the hip of the back or of the neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, then there is no remedy, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the evacuations jump forth without will, nor can he hold it, and many times some member is softened, or both legs or one arm or two.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the hip moves into four parts; that which moves at the back is called "giltosis":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The remedy is that you restore it if the giltosis has come from childhood: if there is no remedy nor healing for all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or beatings or similar things, the ancient manner of cures say by big words, but there is no great benefit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the giltosis which comes at the front of the belly, there is no remedy nor health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly in two sides, and one cannot cure anything except for that which comes at the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be stretched on his back in one place even, and have a strain underneath him, so he does not get hurt.
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then drive one iron stake into the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a bandage around the patient's hips, and thighs, and knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and two ministers know the bandages, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the stake as we have said, and the fingers put their palms on the spine firmly, until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not recover by this cure, then take a board three arms long, and carve a hole underneath the appearance, and have the patient lie on their side, and put the head of the board under the appearance, then place the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and have the fingers put their feet on the other head of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, then do it with the turning wheel that turns at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you drive two stakes at the head of the patient's arm, one long and another short, and have between each stake, outside and underneath, a palm of space about an arm's length;
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and have in each stake one hole, where the turning wheel runs, and be the stakes firmly in the ground, so that they do not move; and between each two stakes be a turning stick, upon which the turning band turns, and have in each two turnings two small sticks of an arm's length, to turn the turning wheel;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the band that is between the hips to the turning wheel towards the head, and the other band towards the feet to the other turning wheel, and each of the ministers turns his wheel around all the band, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, then put on drying ointment with plenty of oil, and then the bandages, and then an ester of a tablet three fingers long that will establish the place of the giltosis and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use gentle massage on the patient, until he is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if nothing comes at the end of healing, then it is necessary to administer soothing and softening medicines, with the ester that we have said before; and sometimes administer one piece of linen.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and sometimes the appearance comes at the back of the spine in the back, and it seems to be dislocation; and it is the bone that opens up, therefore one should not have any presumption about it: by chance it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come to dislocations, not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to .iiii. parts: inward and outward, and before and behind; and more inward than outward, and less dislocated before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and shows more clearly the diseased knee than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot bend their knee at the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the lump that is below the swelling of aposteme hot, because the head of the hip comes away.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it happens outward is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it happens before is that he is well in his leg according to fulfillment; however, he does not bend his knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot beforehand, and retains his urine, and swells with anger, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it happens behind is that he cannot straighten his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the anger is softened, and the head of the hip is at the level below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this likeness of dislocation are that you restore whether the dislocation is old and it remains according to its disposition, if there is no care; and it is not necessary that he have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of the three kinds of dislocation, you hasten to return the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; by chance if it will come back, and there is no need for another care.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not come back in this manner, then it is necessary that you find one strong minister, and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or with one bandage tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another minister stretches his hand above in the same manner that he puts his hands under his armpits, then tightens a soft bandage above the hip; and another ties the end of the bandage.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch up and down all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground all at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of stretching is common to the three likenesses, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, then it is necessary to apply a cure to its likeness. When the dislocation is in the parting, you must soothe the patient on his healthy side, then put the bandage on the root of the hip, and the end which is below the anger, then stretch the bandage upwards towards the anger, and towards the forehead;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then take another minister's arms, and encircle the thick part of the diseased hip, and stretch it outward strongly: if it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot bind it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft bandage on the two heels, and on the two knees, and be the diseased leg stretched two fingers more than the others;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then be hung up on the head of a tree, and be above ground two arms long; then command one minister to encircle the head of the hip, and let another minister hang with the patient, who will encircle strongly the hip, for the jointure returns now hastily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is outward, the patient lies down, as we have said in that one with gilbosity, and stretches a bandage properly over the diseased leg, and also over the belly.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two hot irons, one at the head and another at the feet, then stick one iron between the patient's hips in the middle form;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and let there be placed damp cloths around, so that the patient does not get hurt, then each minister stretches towards him, and the physician puts equal pressure on their hand to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that's good. If not, put them on a table, and press them thus as we have said in gilbosity, and let the patient lie down on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is before, it is necessary to stretch the diseased leg hastily, and according to what I have said; and put the physician's hand on the angry diseased hip, then press with the other hand, and stretch down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is outward, it does not need to be stretched down or lifted up to the ground, but rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated outward, as we have said about lying on two hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and be on their face, and the bandage stretched as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it will be so when the patient stretches their legs and they are equal; then bring together the hips, put the plaster, and stretch with a bandage, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and if it rests three or four days, then loosen it, and put the plaster on; and if you see that they are equal, then stretch, just as before, and leave it. Three days; then loosen it, and make them walk well, until the limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; and does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend their leg to their hip, and if it does not bend to its hip, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and stretch their leg if they can, and put your back on their face, and put their foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take their knee in your palms, and bring it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee strongly; and another minister stretches their foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that they bend their leg gently to their hip.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	et put the poultice on, and make the leg bend at the knee, and bind it together strongly for .iii. days or .iiii., then release it; and do not trouble the patient to walk until the members are comforted.
